# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: typescript_desktop_productivity_expert_055_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: typescript
**Context Length**: 783545 tokens
**Files**: 84

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for Real-Time Collaboration Feature

## Description

PaletteFlow Studio is a successful single-user desktop application for creative and technical professionals. The core value proposition is its infinite canvas where users can place different types of content 'nodes' (text, code, images, etc.) and link them together. The product team has identified real-time multi-user collaboration as the next major strategic feature. The current architecture, based on Electron, was designed exclusively for a single user interacting with a local file system. This task requires the AI agent to act as a software architect, analyzing the existing system to determine the feasibility of this new feature and outline the necessary architectural changes.

## Your Task

You are a principal engineer tasked with creating a technical design document for adding real-time collaboration to PaletteFlow Studio. Before writing the full design, you must first perform a thorough analysis of the current architecture. Your analysis should be presented as a markdown report answering the following key questions. Your answers must be justified by referencing specific files, design patterns, and architectural components in the existing codebase.

### Architectural Analysis Report

1.  **State Management & Source of Truth:**
    -   Where is the primary source of truth for a user's workspace data (nodes, links, content) currently stored?
    -   Describe the current state management strategy in both the main and renderer processes. How do they synchronize?
    -   Explain why this model is or is not suitable for a multi-user real-time environment.

2.  **Data Flow for Mutations:**
    -   Trace the complete data flow when a user performs a simple action, such as moving a node on the canvas in the renderer process, to the point where that change is persisted.
    -   Identify the key components (classes, services, functions) involved in this flow, including the IPC communication layer.
    -   Analyze the limitations of this data flow model in a scenario with multiple concurrent users.

3.  **Impact on the Plugin System:**
    -   The plugin API allows third-party code to read and modify workspace data (e.g., via the Node API described in `docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md`).
    -   How would the introduction of real-time collaboration affect the stability and predictability of the plugin ecosystem?
    -   What specific changes or additions to the plugin API (`IPluginService.ts`, API docs) would be necessary to support a collaborative environment safely?

4.  **Conflict Resolution Strategy:**
    -   Examine the core domain entities (e.g., `Workspace.ts`, `Node.ts`). Do they contain any properties that would support conflict resolution (e.g., version numbers, vector clocks, last-updated timestamps)?
    -   Based on the application's layered architecture (`core`, `adapters`, `main`, `renderer`), where would you recommend implementing the conflict resolution logic (e.g., CRDTs, OT)? Justify your choice.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this analysis systematically:

1.  **High-Level Orientation:** Start by reading `docs/architecture.md` to get a conceptual overview of the system's structure, including the main/renderer process split and the clean architecture principles being used (`core`, `adapters`).

2.  **Identify State Persistence:** Investigate how data is saved. This would lead them to `IWorkspaceRepository.ts` (the interface) and its implementation `FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`. This immediately reveals the local, file-centric nature of the persistence layer.

3.  **Trace a User Action:** To understand data flow, they would pick a user action, like moving a node.
    -   Start in the UI: `renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx` and `Draggable.tsx`.
    -   Follow the state update: This would likely involve a hook (`useViewModel.ts`) that calls a function to update the node's position.
    -   Trace to IPC: The update function would use the IPC bridge (`renderer/ipc/bridge.ts`) to send a message to the main process, likely using a channel defined in `src/main/ipc/channels.ts`.
    -   Trace in Main Process: They would find the corresponding handler in `main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts` or a similar file, which is registered by `IpcMainManager.ts`.
    -   Trace to Core Logic: The IPC handler would invoke a use case, such as `UpdateNodePosition.ts` from `src/core/application/use-cases/`.
    -   Trace to Persistence: The use case would then use the `IWorkspaceRepository` to call the `FileSystemWorkspaceRepository` and write the change to disk.

4.  **Analyze Plugin System:** Review the plugin API documentation (`docs/plugin-api/`) and the core service interface (`IPluginService.ts`). They would note that the APIs likely provide direct, synchronous-style access to data, which is problematic in a distributed system.

5.  **Examine Domain Models:** Open the core entity files like `Node.ts` and `Workspace.ts` to inspect their properties, looking for any metadata related to versioning or synchronization. The absence of such fields is a critical finding.

6.  **Synthesize Findings:** Finally, the developer would combine all these observations to answer the four questions, demonstrating a holistic understanding of how the components interact and why the current design presents significant challenges for real-time collaboration.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Correctly Identifies Architecture:** Accurately describes the Electron main/renderer architecture and the clean architecture layering (`core`, `adapters`).
- **Accurately Traces Data Flow:** Correctly traces the full path of a data mutation from the renderer UI, through the IPC bridge, to the main process handler, and finally to the file system repository.
- **Identifies State Management Flaws:** Correctly identifies the file system as the source of truth and explains why this single-user model is fundamentally incompatible with real-time collaboration.
- **Analyzes IPC Limitations:** Correctly identifies the IPC mechanism as a request-response pattern and explains its inadequacy for broadcasting state to multiple clients.
- **Assesses Plugin API Risks:** Demonstrates understanding of the plugin system's architecture and correctly identifies the risks of synchronous data access in a distributed context.
- **Proposes Correct Locus for Business Logic:** Correctly identifies the `core/application/use-cases` layer as the appropriate location for new conflict resolution logic, justifying the choice based on architectural principles.
- **Synthesizes Information:** The overall quality of the analysis, connecting findings from different files (docs, code, domain models) into a coherent and accurate architectural assessment.

# Architectural Analysis Report: Real-Time Collaboration for PaletteFlow Studio

## Executive Summary

PaletteFlow Studio is a single-user desktop application built on Electron with a Clean Architecture design. This analysis evaluates the feasibility of adding real-time multi-user collaboration and outlines the necessary architectural changes. The current architecture, while well-designed for single-user scenarios, presents significant challenges for collaboration due to its file-system-centric persistence, synchronous plugin APIs, and absence of conflict resolution mechanisms in domain entities.

---

## 1. State Management & Source of Truth

### 1.1 Current Source of Truth

**The primary source of truth for workspace data is the local file system.**

The persistence layer is implemented in `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`:

```typescript
// src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:35-36
const WORKSPACE_FILE_NAME = 'workspace.pfws';  // gzipped JSON
const MANIFEST_FILE_NAME = 'manifest.json';    // plain JSON
```

Each workspace is stored as a gzipped JSON file (`workspace.pfws`) in a directory under the user's configured root. The repository provides:
- **Atomic writes** via write-to-temp-then-rename pattern (lines 147-153)
- **File watching** for external changes (lines 244-255)
- **Event emission** for workspace lifecycle events (lines 276-293)

The `IWorkspaceRepository` interface (`src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts:131-194`) defines the port contract that allows this implementation to be swapped, though currently only the file-system adapter exists.

### 1.2 State Management Strategy

**Main Process:**
- The main process acts as the **orchestration layer** and doesn't
... (truncated)

The solution has been written successfully. Here's a summary of what I've analyzed and documented:

## Summary

I completed a comprehensive architectural analysis of PaletteFlow Studio for real-time collaboration feasibility. The report addresses all four key questions:

### 1. State Management & Source of Truth
- **Current source of truth**: Local file system via `FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`
- **Main process**: Stateless orchestration layer with per-request use cases
- **Renderer process**: Redux Toolkit store with cross-window sync via IPC
- **Assessment**: The file-centric model is fundamentally incompatible with multi-user real-time collaboration due to lack of shared state authority

### 2. Data Flow for Mutations
Traced the complete node movement flow through:
- `NodeComponent.tsx` (UI) → `NodeViewModel` (MobX) → `IPCBridge` (IPC) → `workspaceHandlers.ts` (Main) → `UpdateNodePosition.ts` (Use Case) → `Node.ts` (Entity) → `FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts` (Persistence)

**Limitations identified**: Request-response IPC pattern, sequential save queue, no delta transmission, blocking transactions

### 3. Plugin System Impact
- Current APIs provide synchronous-style data access via `CanvasNodeContext`
- Collaboration would cause stale context problems, hook ordering non-determinism, and event race conditions
- Proposed changes: Versioned state access, optimistic update patterns, presence awareness APIs

### 4. Conflict Resolution Strategy
- **Critical finding**: Domain entities lack conflict resolution metadata (no vector clocks, no operation IDs, only simple `_version` number on Workspace)
- **Recommended location**: `core/application/use-cases` layer for CRDT/OT implementation
- **Justification**: Maintains domain purity, leverages existing repository interfac
... (truncated)

Use-Case Layer (`packages/usecases`)\\n107: \\n108: ### 2.1 Interactor: `CreateNode`\\n109: \\n110: ```ts\\n111: // packages/usecases/CreateNode.ts\\n112: import { NodeFactory } from '../core/factories';\\n113: import { ICanvasRepository } from './ports/ICanvasRepository';\\n114: import { EventBus } from '../core/EventBus';\\n115: \\n116: export interface CreateNodeCommand {\\n117:   canvasId: string;\\n118:   type: string;\\n119:   initialContent?: unknown;\\n120:   position: { x: number; y: number };\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: /**\\n124:  * Use-case for creating a node. Note that it is framework-agnostic and only\\n125:  * depends on abstraction interfaces (`ICanvasRepository`, `EventBus`).\\n126:  */\\n127: export class CreateNode {\\n128:   constructor(\\n129:     private readonly repo: ICanvasRepository,\\n130:     private readonly eventBus: EventBus\\n131:   ) {}\\n132: \\n133:   async execute(cmd: CreateNodeCommand): Promise<void> {\\n134:     const canvas = await this.repo.findById(cmd.canvasId);\\n135:     const node = NodeFactory.create({\\n136:       type: cmd.type,\\n137:       position: cmd.position,\\n138:       content: cmd.initialContent\\n139:     });\\n140: \\n141:     canvas.addNode(node);\\n142: \\n143:     await this.repo.save(canvas);\\n144:     this.eventBus.publish(canvas.toDomainEventStream());\\n145:   }\\n146: }\\n147: ```\\n148: \\n149: ---\\n150: \\n151: ## 3. Adapter Layer\\n152: \\n153: ### 3.1 Electron Renderer \u2192 ViewModel\\n154: \\n155: ```ts\\n156: // packages/desktop/viewmodels/CanvasVM.ts\\n157: import { BehaviorSubject } from 'rxjs';\\n158: import { CreateNode } from '../../usecases';\\n159: import { ipcRenderer } from 'electron';\\n160: \\n161: export class CanvasVM {\\n162:   private readonly state$ = new BehaviorSubject<CanvasState>(initialState);\\n163: \\n164:   constructor(private readonly createNodeUC: CreateNode) {\\n165:     ipcRenderer.on('menu:create-node', (_, payload) => this.createNode(payload));\\n166:   }\\n167: \\n168:   getState() { return this.state$.asObservable(); }\\n169: \\n170:   async createNode(payload: { type: string; x: number; y: number }) {\\n171:     try {\\n172:       await this.createNodeUC.execute({\\n173:         canvasId: this.state$.value.activeCanvasId,\\n174:         type: payload.type,\\n175:         position: { x: payload.x, y: payload.y }\\n176:       });\\n177:     } catch (err) {\\n178:       console.error('[CanvasVM] createNode failed', err);\\n179:       // TODO: route to notifications store\\n180:     }\\n181:   }\\n182: }\\n183: ```\\n184: \\n185: ---\\n186: \\n187: ## 4. Plugin Runtime\\n188: \\n189: Plugins are Node-isolated CommonJS/ESM modules loaded at runtime.  \\n190: They *must* export a `PalettePlugin` that adheres to the following interface:\\n191: \\n192: ```ts\\n193: // packages/plugin-sdk/index.ts\\n194: export interface PalettePlugin {\\n195:   id: string;\\n196:   displayName: string;\\n197:   activate(context: PluginContext): void;\\n198:   deactivate?(): void;\\n199: }\\n200: \\n201: export interface PluginContext {\\n202:   logger: Logger;\\n203:   registerNodeType(definition: NodeTypeDefinition): void;\\n204:   registerTheme(theme: Theme): void;\\n205:   commands: CommandRegistry;\\n206: }\\n207: ```\\n208: \\n209: ### 4.1 Example Plugin `@palettes/sketchNode`\\n210: \\n211: ```ts\\n212: // plugins/sketch-node/index.ts\\n213: import { PalettePlugin } from 'paletteflow/plugin-sdk';\\n214: \\n215: const SketchPlugin: PalettePlugin = {\\n216:   id: 'com.paletteflow.sketch-node',\\n217:   displayName: 'Sketch Node',\\n218:   activate({ registerNodeType, logger }) {\\n219:     logger.info('Activating Sketch Node Plugin');\\n220:     registerNodeType({\\n221:       id: 'sketch',\\n222:       title: 'Sketch',\\n223:       component: async () => import('./SketchNodeRenderer'),\\n224:       initialContent: { paths: [] }\\n225:     });\\n226:   }\\n227: };\\n228: \\n229: export = SketchPlugin;\\n230: ```\\n231: \\n232: Plugins are sandboxed using the [`vm2`](https://github.com/patriksimek/vm2) library, preventing malicious file-system access while still giving useful APIs.\\n233: \\n234: ---\\n235: \\n236: ## 5. State Machine (Node Lifecycle)\\n237: \\n238: Each node has an internal lifecycle expressed as a small `xstate` machine:\\n239: \\n240: ```ts\\n241: // packages/core/statemachines/nodeLifecycle.ts\\n242: import { createMachine, assign } from 'xstate';\\n243: \\n244: interface NodeCtx { dirty: boolean }\\n245: type NodeEvt = { type: 'EDIT' } | { type: 'SAVE_SUCCESS' } | { type: 'SAVE_FAILURE', error: Error };\\n246: \\n247: export const nodeLifecycleMachine = createMachine<NodeCtx, NodeEvt>({\\n248:   id: 'node',\\n249:   initial: 'clean',\\n250:   context: { dirty: false },\\n251:   states: {\\n252:     clean: {\\n253:       on: { EDIT: { target: 'dirty', actions: assign({ dirty: _ => true }) } }\\n254:     },\\n255:     dirty: {\\n256:       invoke: {\\n257:         src: 'saveNode',\\n258:         onDone: { target: 'clean', actions: assign({ dirty: _ => false }) },\\n259:         onError: { target: 'error' }\\n260:       }\\n261:     },\\n262:     error: {\\n263:       entry: ['notifyError'],\\n264:       on: { EDIT: 'dirty' }\\n265:     }\\n266:   }\\n267: });\\n268: ```\\n269: \\n270: ---\\n271: \\n272: ## 6. Event Bus & Observer Pattern\\n273: \\n274: The Event Bus is a thin RxJS subject that bridges domain events to interested adapters:\\n275: \\n276: ```ts\\n277: // packages/core/EventBus.ts\\n278: import { Subject } from 'rxjs';\\n279: \\n280: export type DomainEvent =\\n281:   | { type: 'NodeCreated'; canvasId: string; nodeId: string }\\n282:   | { type: 'ThemeApplied'; workspaceId: string; themeId: string };\\n283: \\n284: export class EventBus {\\n285:   private readonly events$ = new Subject<DomainEvent>();\\n286: \\n287:   publish(events: DomainEvent | DomainEvent[]) {\\n288:     (Array.isArray(events) ? events : [events]).forEach(evt => this.events$.next(evt));\\n289:   }\\n290: \\n291:   subscribe(listener: (evt: DomainEvent) => void) {\\n292:     return this.events$.subscribe(listener);\\n293:   }\\n294: }\\n295: ```\\n296: \\n297: `CrashReporter`, `AutoUpdater`, and `Analytics` are all *observers* that attach to the `EventBus` and perform side-effects such as telemetry or emergency persistence on crash.\\n298: \\n299: ---\\n300: \\n301: ## 7. Error Strategy\\n302: \\n303: Errors **never** leak across layers unwrapped.  \\n304: We employ a unified `Result<T, E>` type with exhaustive switching in callers.\\n305: \\n306: ```ts\\n307: // packages/core/shared/Result.ts\\n308: export type Result<T, E extends Error = Error> =\\n309:   | { ok: true; value: T }\\n310:   | { ok: false; error: E };\\n311: \\n312: export const Result = {\\n313:   ok<T>(value: T): Result<T, never> { return { ok: true, value }; },\\n314:   fail<E extends Error>(error: E): Result<never, E> { return { ok: false, error }; }\\n315: };\\n316: ```\\n317: \\n318: ---\\n319: \\n320: ## 8. Build Pipeline\\n321: \\n322: 1. `pnpm monorepo` workspace \u2192 shares versions, scripts, lockfile.\\n323: 2. `esbuild` for *core* & *use-cases* (fast, tree-shakable).\\n324: 3. `vite` for renderer; `electron-builder` for desktop packaging.\\n325: 4. End-to-end tests via Playwright using the [Electron](https://playwright.dev/docs/api/class-electron) driver.\\n326: 5. Sentry wraps the Electron main and renderer to capture uncaught exceptions.\\n327: \\n328: ---\\n329: \\n330: ## 9. Key Design Decisions\\n331: \\n332: \u2022 Serializable domain events enable *time-travel debugging* and potentially multiplayer sync  \\n333: \u2022 Plugin system purposely kept **non-eval**; each plugin runs in `vm2` or a WebAssembly sandbox  \\n334: \u2022 All state lives in \u201cview-models\u201d \u2192 React components are *pure views*  \\n335: \u2022 No \u201cservice locator\u201d \u2014 dependencies passed via constructors for testability  \\n336: \u2022 Data persistence uses **executable JSON** (`.pflow.jsonc`) that can be inspected & version-controlled  \\n337: \\n338: ---\\n339: \\n340: ## 10. Contribution Workflow\\n341: \\n342: ```\\n343: fork \u2192 feature-branch \u2192 `pnpm test && pnpm lint` \u2192 PR \u2192 code-review (2 approvals) \u2192 squash merge\\n344: ```\\n345: \\n346: Add tests next to code (`*.spec.ts`), prefer property-based strategies for entities\u2019 invariants.\\n347: \\n348: Happy hacking \ud83d\udc9c\\n349: ```\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/locobench-typescript_desktop_productivity_expert_055@6fbe662a17ef183c8455e71ae015165a1024d10f/-/blob/docs/architecture.md\"}",

Use-Case Layer (`packages/usecases`)\n107: \n108: ### 2.1 Interactor: `CreateNode`\n109: \n110: ```ts\n111: // packages/usecases/CreateNode.ts\n112: import { NodeFactory } from '../core/factories';\n113: import { ICanvasRepository } from './ports/ICanvasRepository';\n114: import { EventBus } from '../core/EventBus';\n115: \n116: export interface CreateNodeCommand {\n117:   canvasId: string;\n118:   type: string;\n119:   initialContent?: unknown;\n120:   position: { x: number; y: number };\n121: }\n122: \n123: /**\n124:  * Use-case for creating a node. Note that it is framework-agnostic and only\n125:  * depends on abstraction interfaces (`ICanvasRepository`, `EventBus`).\n126:  */\n127: export class CreateNode {\n128:   constructor(\n129:     private readonly repo: ICanvasRepository,\n130:     private readonly eventBus: EventBus\n131:   ) {}\n132: \n133:   async execute(cmd: CreateNodeCommand): Promise<void> {\n134:     const canvas = await this.repo.findById(cmd.canvasId);\n135:     const node = NodeFactory.create({\n136:       type: cmd.type,\n137:       position: cmd.position,\n138:       content: cmd.initialContent\n139:     });\n140: \n141:     canvas.addNode(node);\n142: \n143:     await this.repo.save(canvas);\n144:     this.eventBus.publish(canvas.toDomainEventStream());\n145:   }\n146: }\n147: ```\n148: \n149: ---\n150: \n151: ## 3. Adapter Layer\n152: \n153: ### 3.1 Electron Renderer \u2192 ViewModel\n154: \n155: ```ts\n156: // packages/desktop/viewmodels/CanvasVM.ts\n157: import { BehaviorSubject } from 'rxjs';\n158: import { CreateNode } from '../../usecases';\n159: import { ipcRenderer } from 'electron';\n160: \n161: export class CanvasVM {\n162:   private readonly state$ = new BehaviorSubject<CanvasState>(initialState);\n163: \n164:   constructor(private readonly createNodeUC: CreateNode) {\n165:     ipcRenderer.on('menu:create-node', (_, payload) => this.createNode(payload));\n166:   }\n167: \n168:   getState() { return this.state$.asObservable(); }\n169: \n170:   async createNode(payload: { type: string; x: number; y: number }) {\n171:     try {\n172:       await this.createNodeUC.execute({\n173:         canvasId: this.state$.value.activeCanvasId,\n174:         type: payload.type,\n175:         position: { x: payload.x, y: payload.y }\n176:       });\n177:     } catch (err) {\n178:       console.error('[CanvasVM] createNode failed', err);\n179:       // TODO: route to notifications store\n180:     }\n181:   }\n182: }\n183: ```\n184: \n185: ---\n186: \n187: ## 4. Plugin Runtime\n188: \n189: Plugins are Node-isolated CommonJS/ESM modules loaded at runtime.  \n190: They *must* export a `PalettePlugin` that adheres to the following interface:\n191: \n192: ```ts\n193: // packages/plugin-sdk/index.ts\n194: export interface PalettePlugin {\n195:   id: string;\n196:   displayName: string;\n197:   activate(context: PluginContext): void;\n198:   deactivate?(): void;\n199: }\n200: \n201: export interface PluginContext {\n202:   logger: Logger;\n203:   registerNodeType(definition: NodeTypeDefinition): void;\n204:   registerTheme(theme: Theme): void;\n205:   commands: CommandRegistry;\n206: }\n207: ```\n208: \n209: ### 4.1 Example Plugin `@palettes/sketchNode`\n210: \n211: ```ts\n212: // plugins/sketch-node/index.ts\n213: import { PalettePlugin } from 'paletteflow/plugin-sdk';\n214: \n215: const SketchPlugin: PalettePlugin = {\n216:   id: 'com.paletteflow.sketch-node',\n217:   displayName: 'Sketch Node',\n218:   activate({ registerNodeType, logger }) {\n219:     logger.info('Activating Sketch Node Plugin');\n220:     registerNodeType({\n221:       id: 'sketch',\n222:       title: 'Sketch',\n223:       component: async () => import('./SketchNodeRenderer'),\n224:       initialContent: { paths: [] }\n225:     });\n226:   }\n227: };\n228: \n229: export = SketchPlugin;\n230: ```\n231: \n232: Plugins are sandboxed using the [`vm2`](https://github.com/patriksimek/vm2) library, preventing malicious file-system access while still giving useful APIs.\n233: \n234: ---\n235: \n236: ## 5. State Machine (Node Lifecycle)\n237: \n238: Each node has an internal lifecycle expressed as a small `xstate` machine:\n239: \n240: ```ts\n241: // packages/core/statemachines/nodeLifecycle.ts\n242: import { createMachine, assign } from 'xstate';\n243: \n244: interface NodeCtx { dirty: boolean }\n245: type NodeEvt = { type: 'EDIT' } | { type: 'SAVE_SUCCESS' } | { type: 'SAVE_FAILURE', error: Error };\n246: \n247: export const nodeLifecycleMachine = createMachine<NodeCtx, NodeEvt>({\n248:   id: 'node',\n249:   initial: 'clean',\n250:   context: { dirty: false },\n251:   states: {\n252:     clean: {\n253:       on: { EDIT: { target: 'dirty', actions: assign({ dirty: _ => true }) } }\n254:     },\n255:     dirty: {\n256:       invoke: {\n257:         src: 'saveNode',\n258:         onDone: { target: 'clean', actions: assign({ dirty: _ => false }) },\n259:         onError: { target: 'error' }\n260:       }\n261:     },\n262:     error: {\n263:       entry: ['notifyError'],\n264:       on: { EDIT: 'dirty' }\n265:     }\n266:   }\n267: });\n268: ```\n269: \n270: ---\n271: \n272: ## 6. Event Bus & Observer Pattern\n273: \n274: The Event Bus is a thin RxJS subject that bridges domain events to interested adapters:\n275: \n276: ```ts\n277: // packages/core/EventBus.ts\n278: import { Subject } from 'rxjs';\n279: \n280: export type DomainEvent =\n281:   | { type: 'NodeCreated'; canvasId: string; nodeId: string }\n282:   | { type: 'ThemeApplied'; workspaceId: string; themeId: string };\n283: \n284: export class EventBus {\n285:   private readonly events$ = new Subject<DomainEvent>();\n286: \n287:   publish(events: DomainEvent | DomainEvent[]) {\n288:     (Array.isArray(events) ? events : [events]).forEach(evt => this.events$.next(evt));\n289:   }\n290: \n291:   subscribe(listener: (evt: DomainEvent) => void) {\n292:     return this.events$.subscribe(listener);\n293:   }\n294: }\n295: ```\n296: \n297: `CrashReporter`, `AutoUpdater`, and `Analytics` are all *observers* that attach to the `EventBus` and perform side-effects such as telemetry or emergency persistence on crash.\n298: \n299: ---\n300: \n301: ## 7. Error Strategy\n302: \n303: Errors **never** leak across layers unwrapped.  \n304: We employ a unified `Result<T, E>` type with exhaustive switching in callers.\n305: \n306: ```ts\n307: // packages/core/shared/Result.ts\n308: export type Result<T, E extends Error = Error> =\n309:   | { ok: true; value: T }\n310:   | { ok: false; error: E };\n311: \n312: export const Result = {\n313:   ok<T>(value: T): Result<T, never> { return { ok: true, value }; },\n314:   fail<E extends Error>(error: E): Result<never, E> { return { ok: false, error }; }\n315: };\n316: ```\n317: \n318: ---\n319: \n320: ## 8. Build Pipeline\n321: \n322: 1. `pnpm monorepo` workspace \u2192 shares versions, scripts, lockfile.\n323: 2. `esbuild` for *core* & *use-cases* (fast, tree-shakable).\n324: 3. `vite` for renderer; `electron-builder` for desktop packaging.\n325: 4. End-to-end tests via Playwright using the [Electron](https://playwright.dev/docs/api/class-electron) driver.\n326: 5. Sentry wraps the Electron main and renderer to capture uncaught exceptions.\n327: \n328: ---\n329: \n330: ## 9. Key Design Decisions\n331: \n332: \u2022 Serializable domain events enable *time-travel debugging* and potentially multiplayer sync  \n333: \u2022 Plugin system purposely kept **non-eval**; each plugin runs in `vm2` or a WebAssembly sandbox  \n334: \u2022 All state lives in \u201cview-models\u201d \u2192 React components are *pure views*  \n335: \u2022 No \u201cservice locator\u201d \u2014 dependencies passed via constructors for testability  \n336: \u2022 Data persistence uses **executable JSON** (`.pflow.jsonc`) that can be inspected & version-controlled  \n337: \n338: ---\n339: \n340: ## 10. Contribution Workflow\n341: \n342: ```\n343: fork \u2192 feature-branch \u2192 `pnpm test && pnpm lint` \u2192 PR \u2192 code-review (2 approvals) \u2192 squash merge\n344: ```\n345: \n346: Add tests next to code (`*.spec.ts`), prefer property-based strategies for entities\u2019 invariants.\n347: \n348: Happy hacking \ud83d\udc9c\n349: ```",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/locobench-typescript_desktop_productivity_expert_055@6fbe662a17ef183c8455e71ae015165a1024d10f/-/blob/docs/architecture.md"
  }
}

stack?: string };\n84:   [RendererToMainChannel.REQUEST_PLUGIN_API] : { pluginId: string };\n85: };\n86: \n87: /**\n88:  * Maps channels to their response values (data returned from main to renderer via `ipcRenderer.invoke`).\n89:  */\n90: type InvokeReturnMap = {\n91:   [RendererToMainChannel.CREATE_NODE]        : { id: string };        // will be cast by caller\n97: };\n98: \n99: /**\n100:  * Maps event channels (push from main to renderer) to event payloads.\n101:  */\n102: type EventPayloadMap = {\n103:   [MainToRendererChannel.NODE_CREATED]       : { id: string; releaseNotes?: string };\n107:   [MainToRendererChannel.CRASH_ACK]          : void;\n108:   [MainToRendererChannel.PLUGIN_API_RESPONSE]: { pluginId: string; api: unknown };\n109: };\n110: \n111: /* --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n112:  * 3. Runtime allow-lists for additional security\n113:  * ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ */\n114: \n115: const INVOKE_CHANNELS = new Set<string>(Object.values(RendererToMainChannel));\n116: const EVENT_CHANNELS  = new Set<string>(Object.values(MainToRendererChannel));\n117: \n118: /* --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n119:  * 4. ------------------------------------------- invoke ------------------------------------------------------------- */\n123:   private static async invoke<\n124:     C extends RendererToMainChannel\n125:   >(channel: C, payload: InvokePayloadMap[C]): Promise<InvokeReturnMap[C]> {\n126:     if (!INVOKE_CHANNELS.has(channel)) {\n127:       throw new Error(`[IPCBridge] Attempt to invoke unauthorized IpcRendererEvent, data: EventPayloadMap[C]) => listener(data);\n144:     ipcRenderer.on(channel, wrapped);\n145: \n146:     // Return unsubscribe function\n147:     return () => \n152:   /* Canvas & Node */\n153:   static async createNode(payload: CreateNodePayload) {\n154:     return IPCBridge.invoke(RendererToMainChannel.CREATE_NODE, payload);\n155:   }\n156: \n157: }\n167: \n168:   static onThemeApplied(\n169:     listener: (data: EventPayloadMap[MainToRendererChannel.THEME_APPLIED]) => void,\n170:   ) {\n171:     return The default (false) is often fine,\n88:    * but some tricky cases (e.g. DOM measurement) may need sync disposal.\n89:    */\n90:   syncDispose?: boolean;\n91: }\n92: \n93: /*******************************************************************************\n94:  * Hook Implementation\n95:  ******************************************************************************/\n96: \n97: /**\n98:  * Typed React hook that spins up any \u201cView-Model-like\u201d object, subscribes the\n99:  * component to its change events through the Concurrent-Mode-safe\n100:  * `useSyncExternalStore`, and disposes the VM on unmount.\n101:  *\n102:  * Usage:\n103:  *\n104:  *   const vm = useViewModel(() => new CanvasPanelVm(deps), [deps]);\n105:  *\n106:  *   // or with state projection:\n107:  *   const { nodes } = useViewModel(\n108:  *     () => new CanvasPanelVm(workspaceId),\n109:  *     [workspaceId],\n110:  *     { selector: (s) => ({ nodes: s.nodes }) }\n111:  *   );\n112:  */\n113: export function useViewModel<S = unknown, VM extends ViewModelLike<S> = ViewModelLike<S>>(\n114:   /**\n115:    * Factory producing a *fresh* View-Model.  It must be referentially-stable\n116:    * across renders, so pass it through `useCallback` if it captures props.\n117:    *\n118:    * IMPORTANT: The factory may throw.  We capture and re-throw after reporting\n119:    * to crash analytics so that the nearest ErrorBoundary handles UI recovery.\n120:    */\n121:   factory: () => VM,\n122:   /**\n123:    * Dependency list that determines when the VM should be recreated.  Follow\n124:    * the exact same rules as `useEffect`\u2019s deps array.\n125:    */\n126:   deps: DependencyList = [],\n127:   /**\n128:    * Additional options.\n129:    */\n130:   options: UseViewModelOptions<S> = {},\n131: ): VM {\n132:   const { selector, equalityFn = Object.is, syncDispose = false } = options;\n133: \n134:   /**\n135:    * The current View-Model instance.\n136:    * `useRef` is OK here because we handle lifecycle manually.\n137:    */\n138:   const vmRef = useRef<VM>();\n139: \n140:   /**\n141:    * Recreate the VM when dependencies change.\n142:    */\n143:   if (vmRef.current === undefined) {\n144:     try {\n145:       vmRef.current = factory();\n146:       if (!vmRef.current) {\n147:         throw new Error('ViewModel factory returned falsy value');\n148:       }\n149:     } catch (err) {\n150:       // Ensure crash analytics capture the context *before* React error boundary\n151:       captureException(err);\n152:       throw err; // Let UI layer handle gracefully\n153:     }\n154:   }\n155: \n156:   /**\n157:    * Compose a stable subscribe/getSnapshot pair required by\n158:    * `useSyncExternalStore`.\n159:    */\n160:   const getSnapshot = useMemo(() => {\n161:     const currentVm = vmRef.current!;\n162:     if (selector) {\n163:       let lastSelected = selector(currentVm.getState());\n164:       return () => {\n165:         const nextSelected = selector(currentVm.getState());\n166:         if (!equalityFn(lastSelected, nextSelected)) {\n167:           lastSelected = nextSelected;\n168:         }\n169:         return lastSelected;\n170:       };\n171:     }\n172:     // no selector; just return raw state\n173:     return () => currentVm.getState();\n174:   }, [selector, equalityFn, ...deps]); // must recompute when deps change\n175: \n176:   const subscribe = useMemo(() => {\n177:     const currentVm = vmRef.current!;\n178:     return (cb: () => void) => currentVm.onChange(cb);\n179:   }, deps); // recreate when VM replaced\n180: \n181:   /**\n182:    * `useSyncExternalStore` handles all\n183:    * \u2013 concurrency edge-cases\n184:    * \u2013 selective re-render\n185:    * \u2013 SSR (not used here but nice to have)\n186:    */\n187:   // eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/rules-of-hooks\n188:   useSyncExternalStore(subscribe, getSnapshot);\n189: \n190:   /**\n191:    * Dispose logic mirror.  We cannot rely on garbage-collection because the VM\n192:    * may hold native handles or global event subscriptions.\n193:    */\n194:   const runDispose = () => {\n195:     const vm = vmRef.current;\n196:     if (vm) {\n197:       try {\n198:         vm.dispose();\n199:       } catch (err) {\n200:         // Disposal should never kill the app; just log\n201:         log.error(err, 'Error during ViewModel.dispose()');\n202:         captureException(err);\n203:       }\n204:       vmRef.current = undefined;\n205:     }\n206:   };\n207: \n208:   const useProperEffect = syncDispose ? useLayoutEffect : useEffect;\n209: \n210:   // eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/rules-of-hooks\n211:   useProperEffect(() => {\n212:     // On deps change \u2192 VM was created earlier in render phase\n213:     return runDispose; // returned callback executes on unmount or deps change\n214:     // deps matches VM lifecycle:\n215:     // eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps\n216:   }, deps);\n217: \n218:   return vmRef.current;\n219: }\n220: \n221: /*******************************************************************************\n222:  * Convenience Overload\n223:  ******************************************************************************/\n224: \n225: /**\n226:  * Overload when caller doesn\u2019t care about selector/equalityFn.\n227:  */\n228: export function useViewModelSimple<S = unknown, VM extends ViewModelLike<S> = ViewModelLike<S>>(\n229:   factory: () => VM,\n230:   deps: DependencyList = [],\n231: ): VM {\n232:   return useViewModel(factory, deps);\n233: }\n234: ```\n235: ",

Should be called during application startup.\n131:      */\n132:     loadEnabledPlugins(): Promise<void>;\n133: \n134:     /**\n135:      * Reloads a single plugin in place without requiring an application restart.\n136:      * Implementations should dispose of the previous execution context before\n137:      * activating the new one.\n138:      */\n139:     reloadPlugin(pluginId: PluginId): Promise<void>;\n140: \n141:     /**\n142:      * Completely unloads all plugins and tears down their execution contexts.\n143:      * Primarily used in unit tests or when changing global security settings.\n144:      */\n145:     unloadAll(): Promise<void>;\n146: \n147:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n148:     // Installation / Uninstallation\n149:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n150: \n151:     /**\n152:      * Installs a plugin from a local .tgz/.zip package.\n153:      *\n154:      * @param packageStream A readable stream containing the plugin archive.\n155:      * @param options       Optional installation parameters.\n156:      * @throws PluginValidationError | PluginConflictError | PluginSecurityError\n157:      */\n158:     installFromStream(\n159:         packageStream: Readable,\n160:         options?: InstallOptions\n161:     ): Promise<InstalledPlugin>;\n162: \n163:     /**\n164:      * Installs a plugin from a remote HTTP(S) URL.\n165:      *\n166:      * The implementation MAY retrieve additional metadata from PaletteFlow\u2019s\n167:      * official Plugin Registry API before downloading the asset.\n168:      */\n169:     installFromUrl(\n170:         url: URL,\n171:         options?: InstallOptions\n172:     ): Promise<InstalledPlugin>;\n173: \n174:     /**\n175:      * Uninstalls a plugin completely.  If the plugin is currently enabled, the\n176:      * service must disable and unload it first.\n177:      *\n178:      * @throws PluginNotFoundError\n179:      */\n180:     uninstall(pluginId: PluginId): Promise<void>;\n181: \n182:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n183:     // Enable / Disable\n184:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n185: \n186:     /**\n187:      * Marks a plugin as enabled and activates it immediately.\n188:      *\n189:      * @throws PluginNotFoundError | PluginValidationError | PluginSecurityError\n190:      */\n191:     enable(pluginId: PluginId): Promise<void>;\n192: \n193:     /**\n194:      * Disables a plugin and unloads its execution context.\n195:      *\n196:      * @throws PluginNotFoundError\n197:      */\n198:     disable(pluginId: PluginId): Promise<void>;\n199: \n200:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n201:     // Queries\n202:     // -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n203: \n204:     /** Returns all plugins currently installed (enabled + disabled). */\n205:     getInstalledPlugins(): Promise<InstalledPlugin[]>;\n206: \n207:     /** Returns only the plugins that are actively enabled and running. */\n208:     getEnabledPlugins(): Promise<InstalledPlugin[]>;\n209: \n210:     /** Convenience helper for fetching a single plugin by its id. */\n211:     getPlugin(pluginId: PluginId): Promise<InstalledPlugin>;\n212: \n213:     // results.\n219:      *\n220:      * Hooks are a type-safe mechanism for plugins to expose functionality to the\n221:      * host application (e.g. \u201cprovideNodeRenderers\u201d, listener A callback that will be invoked synchronously for each event.\n257:      * @returns        A cleanup function for removing the listener.\n258:      */\n259:     subscribe(listener: The page is intentionally exhaustive\u2014every public symbol exposed to\\n7:                plugin authors is documented with rich TypeScript examples, design-guidelines,\\n8:                lifecycle diagrams, and gotchas harvested from real-world usage inside the\\n9:                first-party \u201cPaletteFlow Essentials\u201d plugin bundle.\\n10: -->\\n11: \\n12: # \ud83c\udfa8 PaletteFlow Plugin API \u2014 Node API Reference\\n13: \\n14: A *Node* is the foundational building block of a PaletteFlow canvas.  \\n15: Plugins can register entirely new Node types\u2014Markdown snippets, code run-books, custom\\n16: vector editors, IoT dashboards, \u2026 you name it.\\n17: \\n18: This document teaches you how to:\\n19: \\n20: 1. Declare a custom Node type with rich metadata.  \\n21: 2. Implement a **ViewModel-driven Renderer** that plays nicely with PaletteFlow\u2019s MVVM shell.  \\n22: 3. Wire up a declarative **State Machine** so your Nodes behave predictably and are\\n23:    serializable across workspaces.  \\n24: 4. Expose **Command Palette** actions, a **contextual toolbar**, and participate in global\\n25:    **undo/redo** via the Command pattern.  \\n26: 5. Subscribe to low-level **canvas events** while remaining sandboxed by the plugin host.\\n27: \\n28: All public interfaces shown here are imported from the top-level package\\n29: \\n30: ```ts\\n31: import {\\n32:   CanvasNodeFactory,\\n33:   CanvasNodeRenderer,\\n34:   CanvasNodeContext,\\n35:   registerNodeType,\\n36:   useNodeEvent,\\n37:   CommandRegistrar,\\n38:   NodeStateMachine,\\n39:   NodeLifecycleHooks,\\n40:   Theme,\\n41: } from '@paletteflow/sdk';        // Installed automatically alongside PaletteFlow Studio\\n42: ```\\n43: \\n44: ---\\n45: \\n46: ## 1  Node Metadata\\n47: \\n48: Metadata is a plain object that describes how your Node manifests inside the UX (palette\\n49: search, toolbar icon, import/export, etc.).  It must satisfy the\\n50: `CanvasNodeFactory['meta']` contract:\\n51: \\n52: ```ts\\n53: export interface NodeMeta {\\n54:   type: string;                    // Unique machine-friendly identifier\\n55:   displayName: string;             // Shown in the Command Palette & UI\\n56:   version: string;                 // Semver (should mirror your plugin version)\\n57:   icon?: string | IconComponent;   // 16 \u00d7 16 SVG or React/Vue/Svelte component\\n58:   defaultWidth?: number;           // Initial bounding-box (CSS pixels)\\n59:   defaultHeight?: number;\\n60:   categories?: string[];           // e.g., ['Productivity', 'Visualization']\\n61:   tags?: string[];                 // Free-form search keywords\\n62:   docsUrl?: string;                // Deep-link to your own documentation\\n63: }\\n64: ```\\n65: \\n66: ### Example\\n67: \\n68: ```ts\\n69: const meta: NodeMeta = {\\n70:   type:          'com.acme.stopwatch',\\n71:   displayName:   '\u23f1\ufe0f Stopwatch',\\n72:   version:       '1.2.3',\\n73:   icon:          '<svg \u2026/>',\\n74:   defaultWidth:  320,\\n75:   defaultHeight: 160,\\n76:   categories:    ['Utilities'],\\n77:   tags:          ['time', 'tracking', 'pomodoro'],\\n78:   docsUrl:       'https://acme.dev/paletteflow/stopwatch',\\n79: };\\n80: ```\\n81: \\n82: ---\\n83: \\n84: ## 2  Renderer\\n85: \\n86: PaletteFlow is UI-framework agnostic\u2014your plugin chooses *one* of the officially\\n87: supported renderer runtimes:\\n88: \\n89: \u2022 React 18  \\n90: \u2022 Vue 3  \\n91: \u2022 Svelte 4  \\n92: \u2022 Lit (WebComponents)  \\n93: \u2022 Solid JS  \\n94: \\n95: Renderers must be *purely presentational*. Business logic lives inside the **ViewModel**\\n96: exposed by `CanvasNodeContext.vm`.\\n97: \\n98: Below is a fully-fledged *Stopwatch* Node implemented in React and TypeScript.\\n99: \\n100: ```tsx\\n101: import React, { useEffect } from 'react';\\n102: import { CanvasNodeRenderer, useNodeEvent } from '@paletteflow/sdk/react';\\n103: \\n104: interface StopwatchVm {\\n105:   elapsedMs: number;\\n106:   running: boolean;\\n107:   start: () => void;\\n108:   stop: () => void;\\n109:   reset: () => void;\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: export const StopwatchRenderer: CanvasNodeRenderer<StopwatchVm> = ({\\n113:   ctx,                 // CanvasNodeContext<StopwatchVm>\\n114:   theme,               // Resolved Theme object (colors, fonts, etc.)\\n115: }) => {\\n116:   const { vm } = ctx;\\n117: \\n118:   /* Hot-reloader friendly event subscription */\\n119:   useNodeEvent(ctx, 'themeChanged', (newTheme: Theme) => {\\n120:     console.debug('[Stopwatch] Theme updated \u2192', newTheme.name);\\n121:   });\\n122: \\n123:   // Auto-tick every 100 ms **while** running\\n124:   useEffect(() => {\\n125:     if (!vm.running) return;\\n126: \\n127:     const id = window.setInterval(() => vm.tick?.(), 100);\\n128:     return () => window.clearInterval(id);\\n129:   }, [vm.running]);\\n130: \\n131:   /* \ud83c\udfa8 Dumb component with ZERO business logic */\\n132:   return (\\n133:     <div\\n134:       style={{\\n135:         fontFamily: theme.fontMono,\\n136:         background: theme.surface2,\\n137:         color:      theme.textPrimary,\\n138:         padding:    12,\\n139:         borderRadius: 8,\\n140:         display: 'flex',\\n141:         gap: 8,\\n142:         alignItems: 'center',\\n143:         justifyContent: 'space-between',\\n144:       }}\\n145:     >\\n146:       <span>{(vm.elapsedMs / 1000).toFixed(1)} s</span>\\n147:       {vm.running ? (\\n148:         <button onClick={vm.stop}>Stop</button>\\n149:       ) : (\\n150:         <button onClick={vm.start}>Start</button>\\n151:       )}\\n152:       <button onClick={vm.reset} disabled={vm.elapsedMs === 0}>\\n153:         Reset\\n154:       </button>\\n155:     </div>\\n156:   );\\n157: };\\n158: ```\\n159: \\n160: ---\\n161: \\n162: ## 3  State Machine\\n163: \\n164: Nodes are long-lived and must be serializable.  PaletteFlow relies on XState-inspired\\n165: state machines so your logic is deterministic, testable, and persists cleanly to JSON.\\n166: \\n167: ```ts\\n168: import { NodeStateMachine } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\\n169: \\n170: interface StopwatchState {\\n171:   elapsedMs: number;\\n172: }\\n173: \\n174: interface StopwatchContext {\\n175:   running: boolean;\\n176: }\\n177: \\n178: export const stopwatchMachine: NodeStateMachine<\\n179:   StopwatchState,\\n180:   StopwatchContext\\n181: > = {\\n182:   id: 'stopwatch',\\n183:   context: { running: false },\\n184:   initial: 'idle',\\n185:   states: {\\n186:     idle: {\\n187:       on: {\\n188:         START: { target: 'running', actions: ['startTimer'] },\\n189:       },\\n190:     },\\n191:     running: {\\n192:       on: {\\n193:         STOP: { target: 'idle', actions: ['stopTimer'] },\\n194:         TICK: { actions: ['increment'] },\\n195:       },\\n196:     },\\n197:   },\\n198:   actions: {\\n199:     startTimer: ({ ctx }) => { ctx.running = true; },\\n200:     stopTimer:  ({ ctx }) => { ctx.running = false; },\\n201:     increment:  ({ state }, { ms }) => { state.elapsedMs += ms; },\\n202:   },\\n203:   guards: {\\n204:     hasElapsed: ({ state }) => state.elapsedMs > 0,\\n205:   },\\n206: };\\n207: ```\\n208: \\n209: Action/guard callbacks receive a strongly-typed bag:\\n210: \\n211: ```ts\\n212: type ActionFn<S, C, E extends { type: string }> = (payload: {\\n213:   state: S;          // Mutable clone\\n214:   ctx: C;            // Machine context             (mutable)\\n215:   event: E;          // Raw triggering event\\n216: }) => void;\\n217: ```\\n218: \\n219: ---\\n220: \\n221: ## 4  Canvas Node Factory\\n222: \\n223: Finally, glue the pieces together with `registerNodeType`.\\n224: \\n225: ```ts\\n226: import { registerNodeType, CanvasNodeFactory } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\\n227: import { StopwatchRenderer } from './StopwatchRenderer';\\n228: import { stopwatchMachine }  from './stopwatch.machine';\\n229: import meta                  from './meta.json';\\n230: \\n231: type StopwatchNode = CanvasNodeFactory<\\n232:   typeof stopwatchMachine,\\n233:   StopwatchRenderer\\n234: >;\\n235: \\n236: const stopwatchFactory: StopwatchNode = {\\n237:   meta,\\n238:   machine: stopwatchMachine,\\n239:   renderer: StopwatchRenderer,\\n240: \\n241:   /* Optional lifecycle hooks */\\n242:   hooks: {\\n243:     onCreate(ctx) {\\n244:       ctx.log.debug('Stopwatch created');\\n245:     },\\n246:     onDestroy(ctx) {\\n247:       ctx.log.debug('Stopwatch destroyed');\\n248:     },\\n249:   },\\n250: };\\n251: \\n252: /* Plugin entrypoint \u2014 executed by the host once at load-time */\\n253: export function activate() {\\n254:   registerNodeType(stopwatchFactory);\\n255: }\\n256: ```\\n257: \\n258: > \u26a0\ufe0f The factory itself is **pure metadata**\u2014make sure *none* of the properties capture\\n259: > request-scoped variables (DOM, timers, WebSocket handles, etc.) or you\u2019ll leak memory\\n260: > on hot-reload.\\n261: \\n262: ---\\n263: \\n264: ## 5  Command Palette & Toolbar\\n265: \\n266: PaletteFlow\u2019s global Command Palette (\u21e7\u2318P) can invoke Node-scoped commands declared via\\n267: `CommandRegistrar`.\\n268: \\n269: ```ts\\n270: import { CommandRegistrar } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\\n271: \\n272: export const stopwatchCommands: CommandRegistrar = (ctx) => ({\\n273:   'stopwatch.start': {\\n274:     label: 'Start Stopwatch',\\n275:     when: () => !ctx.vm.running,\\n276:     execute: ctx.vm.start,\\n277:   },\\n278:   'stopwatch.stop': {\\n279:     label: 'Stop Stopwatch',\\n280:     when: () =>  ctx.vm.running,\\n281:     execute: ctx.vm.stop,\\n282:   },\\n283:   'stopwatch.reset': {\\n284:     label: 'Reset Stopwatch',\\n285:     when: () => ctx.vm.elapsedMs > 0,\\n286:     execute: ctx.vm.reset,\\n287:     shortcuts: ['R'],\\n288:   },\\n289: });\\n290: ```\\n291: \\n292: ### Contextual Toolbar\\n293: \\n294: ```ts\\n295: export const toolbar = [\\n296:   {\\n297:     id: 'startStop',\\n298:     icon: '\u25b6\ufe0f/\u23f8\ufe0f',\\n299:     tooltip: (ctx: CanvasNodeContext) => ctx.vm.running ? 'Stop' : 'Start',\\n300:     onClick: (ctx) => ctx.vm.running ? ctx.vm.stop() : ctx.vm.start(),\\n301:   },\\n302:   {\\n303:     id: 'reset',\\n304:     icon: '\u27f2',\\n305:     tooltip: 'Reset (R)',\\n306:     disabled: (ctx) => ctx.vm.elapsedMs === 0,\\n307:     onClick: (ctx) => ctx.vm.reset(),\\n308:   },\\n309: ];\\n310: ```\\n311: \\n312: Register both alongside the Node factory:\\n313: \\n314: ```ts\\n315: registerNodeType({\\n316:   ...stopwatchFactory,\\n317:   commands: stopwatchCommands,\\n318:   toolbar,\\n319: });\\n320: ```\\n321: \\n322: ---\\n323: \\n324: ## 6  Lifecycle Hooks\\n325: \\n326: Hook                   | Timing                                                | Args\\n327: ---------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------ | ----\\n328: `onCreate`             | Right after Node JSON is instantiated (workspace load) | `ctx`\\n329: `onMount`              | Renderer attached to DOM                               | `ctx`\\n330: `onUpdate`             | Renderer re-render; diff contains changed props        | `ctx`, `diff`\\n331: `onDestroy`            | Node removed from canvas or workspace closed           | `ctx`\\n332: \\n333: All hooks receive a **hot-scoped** `CanvasNodeContext`:\\n334: \\n335: ```ts\\n336: interface CanvasNodeContext<VM = any> {\\n337:   readonly id: string;\\n338:   readonly meta: NodeMeta;\\n339:   readonly vm: VM;                       // ViewModel derived from your machine\\n340:   readonly log: Logger;                  // Per-Node logger w/ scoping\\n341:   readonly clipboard: ClipboardAdapter;  // File, text, Node payloads\\n342:   emit<E extends NodeEvent>(event: E): void;\\n343:   on<E extends NodeEvent>(type: E['type'], cb: (event: E) => void): Unsubscribe;\\n344: }\\n345: ```\\n346: \\n347: ---\\n348: \\n349: ## 7  Inter-Node Communication\\n350: \\n351: PaletteFlow ships with *strict* plug-in isolation.  Direct references between Nodes\\n352: inside different plugin sandboxes are forbidden to guarantee hot-reload integrity and\\n353: security.  Instead, use the **Event Bus**:\\n354: \\n355: ```ts\\n356: // sender\\n357: ctx.emit({ type: 'stopwatch/elapsed', ms: ctx.vm.elapsedMs });\\n358: \\n359: // receiver\\n360: useNodeEvent(ctx, 'stopwatch/elapsed', ({ ms }) => {\\n361:   if (ms > 25_000) alert('Take a quick break! \ud83d\udeb6\u200d\u2642\ufe0f');\\n362: });\\n363: ```\\n364: \\n365: Event names are namespaced (`<domain>/<event>`).  Third-party plugins should document\\n366: their contracts in README files.\\n367: \\n368: ---\\n369: \\n370: ## 8  Error Handling\\n371: \\n372: All uncaught exceptions thrown inside Renderers, state-machine actions, commands, or\\n373: lifecycle hooks are wrapped in a plugin-specific boundary and reported through\\n374: PaletteFlow\u2019s crash analytics center.  You can *optionally* attach additional context:\\n375: \\n376: ```ts\\n377: try {\\n378:   riskyOperation();\\n379: } catch (err) {\\n380:   ctx.log.error('Stopwatch tick failed', err, {\\n381:     elapsedMs: ctx.vm.elapsedMs,\\n382:     running:   ctx.vm.running,\\n383:   });\\n384:   throw err;           // Rethrow so host picks it up\\n385: }\\n386: ```\\n387: \\n388: ---\\n389: \\n390: ## 9  Testing & CI\\n391: \\n392: Because Node logic is decoupled from the renderer, you can run fast, headless\\n393: unit-tests with your favorite framework:\\n394: \\n395: ```ts\\n396: // stopwatch.spec.ts\\n397: import { interpretMachine } from '@paletteflow/sdk/testing';\\n398: import { stopwatchMachine } from './stopwatch.machine';\\n399: \\n400: describe('Stopwatch Machine', () => {\\n401:   it('increments elapsedMs while running', () => {\\n402:     const service = interpretMachine(stopwatchMachine).start();\\n403: \\n404:     service.send('START');\\n405:     service.send({ type: 'TICK', ms: 500 });\\n406:     service.send('STOP');\\n407: \\n408:     expect(service.snapshot.state.elapsedMs).toBe(500);\\n409:     expect(service.snapshot.ctx.running).toBe(false);\\n410:   });\\n411: });\\n412: ```\\n413: \\n414: CI pipelines should run `pf validate` to lint meta-schemas and ensure your plugin stays\\n415: forward-compatible with upcoming PaletteFlow Studio releases.\\n416: \\n417: ---\\n418: \\n419: ## 10  Publishing\\n420: \\n421: 1. Add `\\\"paletteflow-plugin\\\": \\\"^1\\\"` to your `package.json` keywords.  \\n422: 2. Run `npm publish --access public`.  \\n423: 3. Submit your plugin URL at <https://paletteflow.io/plugins/submit>.  \\n424: 4. Congrats!  Your Node will appear in users\u2019 in-app discovery feed after automated\\n425:    security scanning (typical SLA \u2264 15 min).\\n426: \\n427: ---\\n428: \\n429: ## 11  API Changelog\\n430: \\n431: Version | Breaking? | Notes\\n432: ------- | --------- | -----\\n433: v2.0    | \u2705        | Renderer props renamed `hostTheme` \u2192 `theme`\\n434: v1.7    |           | Added `toolbar` dynamic disable predicate\\n435: v1.5    |           | Machine guards now access full `canvas` snapshot\\n436: v1.0    |           | Initial GA\\n437: \\n438: Stay tuned via the #plugin-dev Discord channel for release candidates and RFCs.\\n439: \\n440: ---\\n441: \\n442: ## 12  Further Reading\\n443: \\n444: \u2022 [Theme API Reference](./theme-api.md)  \\n445: \u2022 [Plugin Manifest Schema](../manifest-schema.md)  \\n446: \u2022 [PaletteFlow Core Architecture](../../design/architecture.md)\\n447: \\n448: *Happy hacking, and may your canvases flow with infinite creativity!* \ud83d\ude80\\n449: ```\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/locobench-typescript_desktop_productivity_expert_055@6fbe662a17ef183c8455e71ae015165a1024d10f/-/blob/docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md\"}",

Expose **Command Palette** actions, a **contextual toolbar**, and participate in global\n25:    **undo/redo** via the Command pattern.  \n26: 5. Subscribe to low-level **canvas events** while remaining sandboxed by the plugin host.\n27: \n28: All public interfaces shown here are imported from the top-level package\n29: \n30: ```ts\n31: import {\n32:   CanvasNodeFactory,\n33:   CanvasNodeRenderer,\n34:   CanvasNodeContext,\n35:   registerNodeType,\n36:   useNodeEvent,\n37:   CommandRegistrar,\n38:   NodeStateMachine,\n39:   NodeLifecycleHooks,\n40:   Theme,\n41: } from '@paletteflow/sdk';        // Installed automatically alongside PaletteFlow Studio\n42: ```\n43: \n44: ---\n45: \n46: ## 1  Node Metadata\n47: \n48: Metadata is a plain object that describes how your Node manifests inside the UX (palette\n49: search, toolbar icon, import/export, etc.).  It must satisfy the\n50: `CanvasNodeFactory['meta']` contract:\n51: \n52: ```ts\n53: export interface NodeMeta {\n54:   type: string;                    // Unique machine-friendly identifier\n55:   displayName: string;             // Shown in the Command Palette & UI\n56:   version: string;                 // Semver (should mirror your plugin version)\n57:   icon?: string | IconComponent;   // 16 \u00d7 16 SVG or React/Vue/Svelte component\n58:   defaultWidth?: number;           // Initial bounding-box (CSS pixels)\n59:   defaultHeight?: number;\n60:   categories?: string[];           // e.g., ['Productivity', 'Visualization']\n61:   tags?: string[];                 // Free-form search keywords\n62:   docsUrl?: string;                // Deep-link to your own documentation\n63: }\n64: ```\n65: \n66: ### Example\n67: \n68: ```ts\n69: const meta: NodeMeta = {\n70:   type:          'com.acme.stopwatch',\n71:   displayName:   '\u23f1\ufe0f Stopwatch',\n72:   version:       '1.2.3',\n73:   icon:          '<svg \u2026/>',\n74:   defaultWidth:  320,\n75:   defaultHeight: 160,\n76:   categories:    ['Utilities'],\n77:   tags:          ['time', 'tracking', 'pomodoro'],\n78:   docsUrl:       'https://acme.dev/paletteflow/stopwatch',\n79: };\n80: ```\n81: \n82: ---\n83: \n84: ## 2  Renderer\n85: \n86: PaletteFlow is UI-framework agnostic\u2014your plugin chooses *one* of the officially\n87: supported renderer runtimes:\n88: \n89: \u2022 React 18  \n90: \u2022 Vue 3  \n91: \u2022 Svelte 4  \n92: \u2022 Lit (WebComponents)  \n93: \u2022 Solid JS  \n94: \n95: Renderers must be *purely presentational*. Business logic lives inside the **ViewModel**\n96: exposed by `CanvasNodeContext.vm`.\n97: \n98: Below is a fully-fledged *Stopwatch* Node implemented in React and TypeScript.\n99: \n100: ```tsx\n101: import React, { useEffect } from 'react';\n102: import { CanvasNodeRenderer, useNodeEvent } from '@paletteflow/sdk/react';\n103: \n104: interface StopwatchVm {\n105:   elapsedMs: number;\n106:   running: boolean;\n107:   start: () => void;\n108:   stop: () => void;\n109:   reset: () => void;\n110: }\n111: \n112: export const StopwatchRenderer: CanvasNodeRenderer<StopwatchVm> = ({\n113:   ctx,                 // CanvasNodeContext<StopwatchVm>\n114:   theme,               // Resolved Theme object (colors, fonts, etc.)\n115: }) => {\n116:   const { vm } = ctx;\n117: \n118:   /* Hot-reloader friendly event subscription */\n119:   useNodeEvent(ctx, 'themeChanged', (newTheme: Theme) => {\n120:     console.debug('[Stopwatch] Theme updated \u2192', newTheme.name);\n121:   });\n122: \n123:   // Auto-tick every 100 ms **while** running\n124:   useEffect(() => {\n125:     if (!vm.running) return;\n126: \n127:     const id = window.setInterval(() => vm.tick?.(), 100);\n128:     return () => window.clearInterval(id);\n129:   }, [vm.running]);\n130: \n131:   /* \ud83c\udfa8 Dumb component with ZERO business logic */\n132:   return (\n133:     <div\n134:       style={{\n135:         fontFamily: theme.fontMono,\n136:         background: theme.surface2,\n137:         color:      theme.textPrimary,\n138:         padding:    12,\n139:         borderRadius: 8,\n140:         display: 'flex',\n141:         gap: 8,\n142:         alignItems: 'center',\n143:         justifyContent: 'space-between',\n144:       }}\n145:     >\n146:       <span>{(vm.elapsedMs / 1000).toFixed(1)} s</span>\n147:       {vm.running ? (\n148:         <button onClick={vm.stop}>Stop</button>\n149:       ) : (\n150:         <button onClick={vm.start}>Start</button>\n151:       )}\n152:       <button onClick={vm.reset} disabled={vm.elapsedMs === 0}>\n153:         Reset\n154:       </button>\n155:     </div>\n156:   );\n157: };\n158: ```\n159: \n160: ---\n161: \n162: ## 3  State Machine\n163: \n164: Nodes are long-lived and must be serializable.  PaletteFlow relies on XState-inspired\n165: state machines so your logic is deterministic, testable, and persists cleanly to JSON.\n166: \n167: ```ts\n168: import { NodeStateMachine } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\n169: \n170: interface StopwatchState {\n171:   elapsedMs: number;\n172: }\n173: \n174: interface StopwatchContext {\n175:   running: boolean;\n176: }\n177: \n178: export const stopwatchMachine: NodeStateMachine<\n179:   StopwatchState,\n180:   StopwatchContext\n181: > = {\n182:   id: 'stopwatch',\n183:   context: { running: false },\n184:   initial: 'idle',\n185:   states: {\n186:     idle: {\n187:       on: {\n188:         START: { target: 'running', actions: ['startTimer'] },\n189:       },\n190:     },\n191:     running: {\n192:       on: {\n193:         STOP: { target: 'idle', actions: ['stopTimer'] },\n194:         TICK: { actions: ['increment'] },\n195:       },\n196:     },\n197:   },\n198:   actions: {\n199:     startTimer: ({ ctx }) => { ctx.running = true; },\n200:     stopTimer:  ({ ctx }) => { ctx.running = false; },\n201:     increment:  ({ state }, { ms }) => { state.elapsedMs += ms; },\n202:   },\n203:   guards: {\n204:     hasElapsed: ({ state }) => state.elapsedMs > 0,\n205:   },\n206: };\n207: ```\n208: \n209: Action/guard callbacks receive a strongly-typed bag:\n210: \n211: ```ts\n212: type ActionFn<S, C, E extends { type: string }> = (payload: {\n213:   state: S;          // Mutable clone\n214:   ctx: C;            // Machine context             (mutable)\n215:   event: E;          // Raw triggering event\n216: }) => void;\n217: ```\n218: \n219: ---\n220: \n221: ## 4  Canvas Node Factory\n222: \n223: Finally, glue the pieces together with `registerNodeType`.\n224: \n225: ```ts\n226: import { registerNodeType, CanvasNodeFactory } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\n227: import { StopwatchRenderer } from './StopwatchRenderer';\n228: import { stopwatchMachine }  from './stopwatch.machine';\n229: import meta                  from './meta.json';\n230: \n231: type StopwatchNode = CanvasNodeFactory<\n232:   typeof stopwatchMachine,\n233:   StopwatchRenderer\n234: >;\n235: \n236: const stopwatchFactory: StopwatchNode = {\n237:   meta,\n238:   machine: stopwatchMachine,\n239:   renderer: StopwatchRenderer,\n240: \n241:   /* Optional lifecycle hooks */\n242:   hooks: {\n243:     onCreate(ctx) {\n244:       ctx.log.debug('Stopwatch created');\n245:     },\n246:     onDestroy(ctx) {\n247:       ctx.log.debug('Stopwatch destroyed');\n248:     },\n249:   },\n250: };\n251: \n252: /* Plugin entrypoint \u2014 executed by the host once at load-time */\n253: export function activate() {\n254:   registerNodeType(stopwatchFactory);\n255: }\n256: ```\n257: \n258: > \u26a0\ufe0f The factory itself is **pure metadata**\u2014make sure *none* of the properties capture\n259: > request-scoped variables (DOM, timers, WebSocket handles, etc.) or you\u2019ll leak memory\n260: > on hot-reload.\n261: \n262: ---\n263: \n264: ## 5  Command Palette & Toolbar\n265: \n266: PaletteFlow\u2019s global Command Palette (\u21e7\u2318P) can invoke Node-scoped commands declared via\n267: `CommandRegistrar`.\n268: \n269: ```ts\n270: import { CommandRegistrar } from '@paletteflow/sdk';\n271: \n272: export const stopwatchCommands: CommandRegistrar = (ctx) => ({\n273:   'stopwatch.start': {\n274:     label: 'Start Stopwatch',\n275:     when: () => !ctx.vm.running,\n276:     execute: ctx.vm.start,\n277:   },\n278:   'stopwatch.stop': {\n279:     label: 'Stop Stopwatch',\n280:     when: () =>  ctx.vm.running,\n281:     execute: ctx.vm.stop,\n282:   },\n283:   'stopwatch.reset': {\n284:     label: 'Reset Stopwatch',\n285:     when: () => ctx.vm.elapsedMs > 0,\n286:     execute: ctx.vm.reset,\n287:     shortcuts: ['R'],\n288:   },\n289: });\n290: ```\n291: \n292: ### Contextual Toolbar\n293: \n294: ```ts\n295: export const toolbar = [\n296:   {\n297:     id: 'startStop',\n298:     icon: '\u25b6\ufe0f/\u23f8\ufe0f',\n299:     tooltip: (ctx: CanvasNodeContext) => ctx.vm.running ? 'Stop' : 'Start',\n300:     onClick: (ctx) => ctx.vm.running ? ctx.vm.stop() : ctx.vm.start(),\n301:   },\n302:   {\n303:     id: 'reset',\n304:     icon: '\u27f2',\n305:     tooltip: 'Reset (R)',\n306:     disabled: (ctx) => ctx.vm.elapsedMs === 0,\n307:     onClick: (ctx) => ctx.vm.reset(),\n308:   },\n309: ];\n310: ```\n311: \n312: Register both alongside the Node factory:\n313: \n314: ```ts\n315: registerNodeType({\n316:   ...stopwatchFactory,\n317:   commands: stopwatchCommands,\n318:   toolbar,\n319: });\n320: ```\n321: \n322: ---\n323: \n324: ## 6  Lifecycle Hooks\n325: \n326: Hook                   | Timing                                                | Args\n327: ---------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------ | ----\n328: `onCreate`             | Right after Node JSON is instantiated (workspace load) | `ctx`\n329: `onMount`              | Renderer attached to DOM                               | `ctx`\n330: `onUpdate`             | Renderer re-render; diff contains changed props        | `ctx`, `diff`\n331: `onDestroy`            | Node removed from canvas or workspace closed           | `ctx`\n332: \n333: All hooks receive a **hot-scoped** `CanvasNodeContext`:\n334: \n335: ```ts\n336: interface CanvasNodeContext<VM = any> {\n337:   readonly id: string;\n338:   readonly meta: NodeMeta;\n339:   readonly vm: VM;                       // ViewModel derived from your machine\n340:   readonly log: Logger;                  // Per-Node logger w/ scoping\n341:   readonly clipboard: ClipboardAdapter;  // File, text, Node payloads\n342:   emit<E extends NodeEvent>(event: E): void;\n343:   on<E extends NodeEvent>(type: E['type'], cb: (event: E) => void): Unsubscribe;\n344: }\n345: ```\n346: \n347: ---\n348: \n349: ## 7  Inter-Node Communication\n350: \n351: PaletteFlow ships with *strict* plug-in isolation.  Direct references between Nodes\n352: inside different plugin sandboxes are forbidden to guarantee hot-reload integrity and\n353: security.  Instead, use the **Event Bus**:\n354: \n355: ```ts\n356: // sender\n357: ctx.emit({ type: 'stopwatch/elapsed', ms: ctx.vm.elapsedMs });\n358: \n359: // receiver\n360: useNodeEvent(ctx, 'stopwatch/elapsed', ({ ms }) => {\n361:   if (ms > 25_000) alert('Take a quick break! \ud83d\udeb6\u200d\u2642\ufe0f');\n362: });\n363: ```\n364: \n365: Event names are namespaced (`<domain>/<event>`).  Third-party plugins should document\n366: their contracts in README files.\n367: \n368: ---\n369: \n370: ## 8  Error Handling\n371: \n372: All uncaught exceptions thrown inside Renderers, state-machine actions, commands, or\n373: lifecycle hooks are wrapped in a plugin-specific boundary and reported through\n374: PaletteFlow\u2019s crash analytics center.  You can *optionally* attach additional context:\n375: \n376: ```ts\n377: try {\n378:   riskyOperation();\n379: } catch (err) {\n380:   ctx.log.error('Stopwatch tick failed', err, {\n381:     elapsedMs: ctx.vm.elapsedMs,\n382:     running:   ctx.vm.running,\n383:   });\n384:   throw err;           // Rethrow so host picks it up\n385: }\n386: ```\n387: \n388: ---\n389: \n390: ## 9  Testing & CI\n391: \n392: Because Node logic is decoupled from the renderer, you can run fast, headless\n393: unit-tests with your favorite framework:\n394: \n395: ```ts\n396: // stopwatch.spec.ts\n397: import { interpretMachine } from '@paletteflow/sdk/testing';\n398: import { stopwatchMachine } from './stopwatch.machine';\n399: \n400: describe('Stopwatch Machine', () => {\n401:   it('increments elapsedMs while running', () => {\n402:     const service = interpretMachine(stopwatchMachine).start();\n403: \n404:     service.send('START');\n405:     service.send({ type: 'TICK', ms: 500 });\n406:     service.send('STOP');\n407: \n408:     expect(service.snapshot.state.elapsedMs).toBe(500);\n409:     expect(service.snapshot.ctx.running).toBe(false);\n410:   });\n411: });\n412: ```\n413: \n414: CI pipelines should run `pf validate` to lint meta-schemas and ensure your plugin stays\n415: forward-compatible with upcoming PaletteFlow Studio releases.\n416: \n417: ---\n418: \n419: ## 10  Publishing\n420: \n421: 1. Add `\"paletteflow-plugin\": \"^1\"` to your `package.json` keywords.  \n422: 2. Run `npm publish --access public`.  \n423: 3. Submit your plugin URL at <https://paletteflow.io/plugins/submit>.  \n424: 4. Congrats!  Your Node will appear in users\u2019 in-app discovery feed after automated\n425:    security scanning (typical SLA \u2264 15 min).\n426: \n427: ---\n428: \n429: ## 11  API Changelog\n430: \n431: Version | Breaking? | Notes\n432: ------- | --------- | -----\n433: v2.0    | \u2705        | Renderer props renamed `hostTheme` \u2192 `theme`\n434: v1.7    |           | Added `toolbar` dynamic disable predicate\n435: v1.5    |           | Machine guards now access full `canvas` snapshot\n436: v1.0    |           | Initial GA\n437: \n438: Stay tuned via the #plugin-dev Discord channel for release candidates and RFCs.\n439: \n440: ---\n441: \n442: ## 12  Further Reading\n443: \n444: \u2022 [Theme API Reference](./theme-api.md)  \n445: \u2022 [Plugin Manifest Schema](../manifest-schema.md)  \n446: \u2022 [PaletteFlow Core Architecture](../../design/architecture.md)\n447: \n448: *Happy hacking, and may your canvases flow with infinite creativity!* \ud83d\ude80\n449: ```",

Handlers MAY return a promise;\n66:  * failures will be captured and forwarded to the bus logger.\n67:  */\n68: export type EventHandler<E extends DomainEvent = DomainEvent> = (\n69:   event: E,\n70: ) => void | Promise<void>;\n71: \n72: export interface Subscription {\n73:   /** Opaque ID that can be used to unsubscribe programmatically */\n74:   readonly id: string;\n75: \n76:   /** Cancels the underlying handler */\n77:   unsubscribe(): void;\n78: }\n79: \n80: /**\n81:  * Options that influence how an event is dispatched.\n82:  */\n83: export interface PublishOptions {\n84:   /**\n85:    * If `true`, events will be delivered synchronously in the caller\u2019s\n86:    * call stack.  This is handy for tests but **must** be `false` in any\n87:    * user-facing UI thread to avoid jank / re-entrance bugs.\n88:    *\n89:    * Defaults to `false`.\n90:    */\n91:   readonly sync?: boolean;\n92: }\n93: \n94: /**\n95:  * Clean-Architecture friendly abstraction that decouples all layers\n96:  * from any specific eventing library (EventEmitter, RxJS, etc.).\n97:  */\n98: export interface IEventBus {\n99:   /**\n100:    * Broadcast a single event to all interested handlers.\n101:    */\n102:   publish<E extends DomainEvent>(\n103:     event: E,\n104:     options?: PublishOptions,\n105:   ): Promise<void>;\n106: \n107:   /**\n108:    * Publish multiple events atomically.  An implementation MAY ensure\n109:    * transactional guarantees (e.g. either all or none are dispatched),\n110:    * but the default in-memory variant does **not**.\n111:    */\n112:   publishAll(events: ReadonlyArray<DomainEvent>, options?: PublishOptions): Promise<void>;\n113: \n114:   /**\n115:    * Register a new handler for the given event type.\n116:    *\n117:    * eventType may be:\n118:    *   \u2022 a concrete string\n119:    *   \u2022 the wildcard \"*\" for all events\n120:    */\n121:   subscribe<E extends DomainEvent>(\n122:     eventType: string,\n123:     handler: EventHandler<E>,\n124:   ): Subscription;\n125: \n126:   /**\n127:    * Convenience helper to run a handler only once.  The subscription\n128:    * self-destructs after the first invocation.\n129:    */\n130:   once<E extends DomainEvent>(\n131:     eventType: string,\n132:     handler: EventHandler<E>,\n133:   ): Subscription;\n134: \n135:   /**\n136:    * Remove a previously registered subscription.\n137:    */\n138:   unsubscribe(subscriptionId: string): void;\n139: \n140:   /**\n141:    * Removes all handlers \u2013 handy for test tear-down or hot-module reloads.\n142:    */\n143:   drain(): void;\n144: }\n145: \n146: /* ------------------------------------------------------------------\n147:  * Reference implementation \u2013 In-Memory, Single-Process\n148:  * ------------------------------------------------------------------ */\n149: \n150: export class InMemoryEventBus implements IEventBus {\n151:   private readonly handlers: Map<\n152:     string, // eventType\n153:     Map<string, EventHandler> // subscriptionId -> handler\n154:   > = new Map();\n155: \n156:   private readonly logger: Pick<Console, 'debug' | 'error'>;\n157: \n158:   constructor(logger: Pick<Console, 'debug' | 'error'> = console) {\n159:     this.logger = logger;\n160:   }\n161: \n162:   /* ---------------------------------- publish ---------------------------------- */\n163: \n164:   async publish<E extends DomainEvent>(\n165:     event: E,\n166:     options: PublishOptions = {},\n167:   ): Promise<void> {\n168:     await this.dispatch([event], options);\n169:   }\n170: \n171:   async publishAll(\n172:     events: ReadonlyArray<DomainEvent>,\n173:     options: PublishOptions = {},\n174:   ): Promise<void> {\n175:     await this.dispatch(events, options);\n176:   }\n177: \n178:   /* -------------------------------- subscribe --------------------------------- */\n179: \n180: a non-empty string');\n186:     }\n187:     if (typeof handler !== 'function') {\n188:       throw new Error('handler must be a function');\n189:     }\n190: \n191:     const subscriptionId = uuid();\n192: \n193:     if (!this.handlers.has(eventType)) {\n194:       this.handlers.set(eventType, new Map());\n195:     }\n196:     this.handlers.get(eventType)!.set(subscriptionId, handler);\n197: \n198:     return {\n199:       id: subscriptionId,\n200:       unsubscribe: () => this.unsubscribe(subscriptionId),\n201:     };\n202:   }\n203: \n204:   once<E extends  }\n219: \n220:   /* ------------------------------ unsubscribe ---------------------------------- */\n221: \n222:   unsubscribe(subscriptionId: string): void {\n223:     for (const [, subs] of this.handlers) {\n224:       if (subs.delete(subscriptionId)) {\n225:         return;\n226:       }\n227:     }\n228:   }\n229: \n230:   drain(): void {\n231:     this.handlers.clear();\n232:   }\n233: \n234:   /* ------------------------------------------------------------------ helpers */\n235: \n236:   private async dispatch(\n237:     events: ReadonlyArray<DomainEvent>,\n238:     { sync event.type, event);\n244:       const matchedHandlers = [\n245:         ...(this.handlers.get('*')?.values() ?? []),\n246:         ...(this.handlers.get(event.type)?.values() ?? []),\n247:       ];\n248: \n249:       for (const handler of matchedHandlers) {\n250:         const invoke = () =>\n251:           Promise.resolve()\n252:             .then(() => handler(event))\n253:             .catch((err) => {\n254:               this.logger.error(\n255:                 `[EventBus] Handler threw for event \"${event.type}\"`,\n256:                 err,\n257:               );\n258:             });\n259: \n260:         if (sync) {\n261:           // Execute immediately (still async to allow error capturing)\n262:           deliveries.push(invoke());\n263:         } else {\n264:           // Defer so we never block the caller\n265:           deliveries.push(queueMicrotaskPolyfill(invoke));\n266:         }\n267:       }\n268:     }\n269: \n270:     await Promise.all(deliveries);\n271:   }\n272: }\n273: \n274: /**\n275:  * queueMicrotask is not available in all Node versions that our\n276:  * CLI adapters support.
