  "content": "# Architectural Analysis Report: Real-Time Collaboration for PaletteFlow Studio\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nPaletteFlow Studio is a single-user desktop application built on Electron with a Clean Architecture design. This analysis evaluates the feasibility of adding real-time multi-user collaboration and outlines the necessary architectural changes. The current architecture, while well-designed for single-user scenarios, presents significant challenges for collaboration due to its file-system-centric persistence, synchronous plugin APIs, and absence of conflict resolution mechanisms in domain entities.\n\n---\n\n## 1. State Management & Source of Truth\n\n### 1.1 Current Source of Truth\n\n**The primary source of truth for workspace data is the local file system.**\n\nThe persistence layer is implemented in `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`:\n\n```typescript\n// src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:35-36\nconst WORKSPACE_FILE_NAME = 'workspace.pfws';  // gzipped JSON\nconst MANIFEST_FILE_NAME = 'manifest.json';    // plain JSON\n```\n\nEach workspace is stored as a gzipped JSON file (`workspace.pfws`) in a directory under the user's configured root. The repository provides:\n- **Atomic writes** via write-to-temp-then-rename pattern (lines 147-153)\n- **File watching** for external changes (lines 244-255)\n- **Event emission** for workspace lifecycle events (lines 276-293)\n\nThe `IWorkspaceRepository` interface (`src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts:131-194`) defines the port contract that allows this implementation to be swapped, though currently only the file-system adapter exists.\n\n### 1.2 State Management Strategy\n\n**Main Process:**\n- The main process acts as the **orchestration layer** and doesn't maintain significant application state\n- Use cases are instantiated per-request in IPC handlers (`src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts:85-86`)\n- State flows through the repository layer to the file system\n- Domain events are published via `DomainEventBus` for cross-cutting concerns\n\n**Renderer Process:**\n- Uses **Redux Toolkit** with the store defined in `src/renderer/state/store.ts`\n- The store holds UI-centric slices: `workspace`, `ui`, and `pluginHub` (lines 71-75)\n- State synchronization happens via:\n  1. **Cross-window middleware** (`crossWindowSyncMiddleware`, lines 154-173) that broadcasts Redux actions via IPC\n  2. **IPC listener** for `main:action-broadcast` that re-dispatches actions from other windows (lines 243-250)\n  3. **State replacement** mechanism via `main:state-replace` for loading workspace files (lines 257-263)\n\n**Synchronization Mechanism:**\nThe current sync is **event-driven but eventually consistent**:\n```typescript\n// src/renderer/state/store.ts:243-250\nipcRenderer.on(\n  'main:action-broadcast',\n  (_: IpcRendererEvent, { originId, action }) => {\n    if (originId !== window.__WINDOW_ID__) {\n      store.dispatch(action as AnyAction);\n    }\n  }\n);\n```\n\n### 1.3 Suitability for Multi-User Real-Time Environment\n\n**This model is NOT suitable for real-time collaboration for several reasons:**\n\n1. **Single-Point File Lock**: The file system cannot serve as a shared source of truth for multiple simultaneous users. File-level locking (mentioned at line 77: \"Basic optimistic locking to avoid clobbering concurrent saves\") only works within a single machine.\n\n2. **No Server-Side Authority**: There is no central server to act as the authoritative state holder. Each user's local file system is their truth, creating inevitable divergence.\n\n3. **Stale Read Problem**: When User A modifies a node, User B's renderer process has no mechanism to receive that update - the file system watcher only monitors local changes.\n\n4. **No Ordering Guarantees**: The Redux action broadcasting assumes all participants receive actions in the same order, which cannot be guaranteed across network boundaries.\n\n5. **Optimistic Updates Without Rollback**: The current optimistic concurrency control (`WorkspaceConflictError` in `IWorkspaceRepository.ts:100-104`) is designed for local multi-window scenarios, not distributed conflict detection.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Data Flow for Mutations\n\n### 2.1 Tracing a Node Move Operation\n\nLet's trace the complete data flow when a user drags a node on the canvas:\n\n#### Step 1: UI Event Capture (Renderer - React Component)\n\n**File:** `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx:120-126`\n\n```typescript\nconst handlePointerMove = useCallback<React.PointerEventHandler<HTMLDivElement>>(\n  (e) => {\n    if (!isDragging) return;\n    nodeVM.setPosition(e.clientX - dragOrigin.current.x, e.clientY - dragOrigin.current.y);\n  },\n  [isDragging, nodeVM],\n);\n```\n\nThe `NodeComponent` captures pointer events and calls `nodeVM.setPosition()` on the ViewModel.\n\n#### Step 2: ViewModel Update (Renderer - MobX Observable)\n\n**File:** Referenced as `NodeViewModel` from `src/renderer/viewModels/NodeViewModel`\n\nThe ViewModel (likely MobX-based given the `observer` wrapper at line 243) updates its internal observable state and triggers a re-render.\n\n#### Step 3: IPC Bridge Call (Renderer to Main)\n\nThe ViewModel calls through the IPC bridge. Based on the bridge structure (`src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts`), a node position update would invoke something like:\n\n```typescript\n// src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts - Pattern for canvas operations\nipcRenderer.invoke(channel, payload)\n```\n\n#### Step 4: IPC Handler Reception (Main Process)\n\n**File:** `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts`\n\nThe handler receives the request and instantiates the appropriate use case.\n\n#### Step 5: Use Case Execution (Core Application Layer)\n\n**File:** `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts:108-183`\n\n```typescript\nasync execute(dto: UpdateNodePositionDTO): Promise<Result<UpdateNodePositionError, void>> {\n    // Validation\n    if (!this.isFiniteCoordinate(dto.x, dto.y)) { ... }\n\n    // Fetch entities\n    const canvas = await this.canvasRepo.findById(dto.canvasId);\n    const node = await this.nodeRepo.findById(dto.nodeId);\n\n    // Plugin hook for veto/transformation\n    const pluginDisposition = await this.pluginHost.hooks.beforeNodeMove.reduce(...);\n\n    // Execute in transaction\n    await this.tx.runInTransaction(async () => {\n        node.moveTo(pluginDisposition.x, pluginDisposition.y);\n        await this.nodeRepo.save(node);\n\n        // Publish domain event\n        await this.eventBus.publish(new NodePositionUpdated({...}));\n    });\n\n    // Post-move plugin hooks\n    await this.pluginHost.hooks.afterNodeMove.forEach(...);\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Domain Entity Mutation\n\n**File:** `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts:223-230`\n\n```typescript\npublic moveTo(position: Vector2D): this {\n    if (Number.isNaN(position.x) || Number.isNaN(position.y)) {\n        throw new Error('Position must contain valid numbers.');\n    }\n    this._position = { x: position.x, y: position.y };\n    this._touch();  // Updates metadata.updatedAt\n    return this._registerEvent('NodeMoved', { position: this._position });\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Repository Persistence\n\n**File:** `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:132-174`\n\nThe `save()` method:\n1. Creates workspace directory if needed\n2. Serializes workspace to JSON\n3. Compresses with gzip\n4. Writes atomically via temp file + rename\n\n#### Step 8: Domain Event Propagation\n\n**File:** `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts:102-105`\n\n```typescript\npublish<E extends DomainEvent>(\n  event: E,\n  options?: PublishOptions,\n): Promise<void>;\n```\n\nThe `NodePositionUpdated` event is broadcast to subscribers (analytics, plugin SDK, UI observers).\n\n### 2.2 Key Components Summary\n\n| Layer | Component | File Path |\n|-------|-----------|-----------|\n| UI | NodeComponent | `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx` |\n| ViewModel | NodeViewModel | `src/renderer/viewModels/NodeViewModel` |\n| IPC Bridge | IPCBridge | `src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts` |\n| IPC Handler | workspaceHandlers | `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts` |\n| Use Case | UpdateNodePosition | `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts` |\n| Domain Entity | Node | `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts` |\n| Repository Port | IWorkspaceRepository | `src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Repository Impl | FileSystemWorkspaceRepository | `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Event Bus | IEventBus | `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts` |\n\n### 2.3 Limitations for Concurrent Users\n\n1. **Request-Response IPC Model**: The current `ipcMain.handle()` / `ipcRenderer.invoke()` pattern (`src/main/ipc/channels.ts:176`) is designed for single-client request-response. There's no built-in mechanism for the main process to push updates to renderers that didn't initiate the request.\n\n2. **Sequential Save Queue**: The `saveQueue` in `workspaceHandlers.ts:50-51` serializes saves per workspace, but only within a single main process. Multiple users would bypass this queue.\n\n3. **No Delta Transmission**: The entire workspace is serialized and persisted on each save. For collaboration, we'd need operation-level (delta) transmission.\n\n4. **Blocking Transactions**: The `TransactionManager` used in `UpdateNodePosition.ts:156-169` provides local atomicity but cannot coordinate distributed transactions.\n\n5. **Plugin Veto Race Conditions**: The `beforeNodeMove` hook (line 142-152) runs sequentially through plugins. In a multi-user scenario, Plugin A might veto User A's move while simultaneously allowing User B's conflicting move.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Impact on the Plugin System\n\n### 3.1 Current Plugin API Architecture\n\nThe plugin system is defined through:\n- **Service Interface:** `src/core/application/services/IPluginService.ts`\n- **SDK Documentation:** `docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md`\n\nKey characteristics:\n\n1. **Synchronous-Style Data Access**: The Node API (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:336-344`) provides direct access to ViewModel state:\n   ```typescript\n   interface CanvasNodeContext<VM = any> {\n     readonly id: string;\n     readonly vm: VM;  // Direct ViewModel access\n     emit<E extends NodeEvent>(event: E): void;\n     on<E extends NodeEvent>(type: E['type'], cb: (event: E) => void): Unsubscribe;\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Hook-Based Extension**: Plugins implement lifecycle hooks (`onCreate`, `onMount`, `onUpdate`, `onDestroy`) that receive a \"hot-scoped\" context (line 333-344).\n\n3. **State Machine Pattern**: Node logic is encapsulated in XState-inspired machines (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:178-206`) with mutable context.\n\n4. **Sandboxed Execution**: Plugins run in `vm2` sandboxes per the architecture doc (line 232).\n\n### 3.2 Collaboration Impact on Plugin Stability\n\n**The introduction of real-time collaboration would significantly destabilize the plugin ecosystem:**\n\n1. **Stale Context Problem**: The `CanvasNodeContext.vm` reference assumes stable, locally-controlled state. With collaboration:\n   ```typescript\n   // Plugin code\n   const oldPosition = ctx.vm.position;  // {x: 100, y: 100}\n   // ... another user moves the node remotely ...\n   ctx.vm.updateContent(...);  // Operates on stale position assumption\n   ```\n\n2. **Hook Ordering Non-Determinism**: The `beforeNodeMove` reducer pattern (from `UpdateNodePosition.ts:142-144`) assumes sequential plugin execution. With concurrent users, two hooks might run on different initial states:\n   ```typescript\n   // Current single-user flow\n   pluginHost.hooks.beforeNodeMove.reduce(\n     async (incomingPosition, hook) => hook(node, await incomingPosition),\n     Promise.resolve({ x: dto.x, y: dto.y })\n   );\n   ```\n\n3. **Event Race Conditions**: The event bus (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:356-366`) uses namespaced events for inter-node communication. Concurrent modifications could trigger event storms or out-of-order delivery.\n\n4. **State Machine Divergence**: The `NodeStateMachine` pattern expects deterministic state transitions. Remote operations could cause local machines to receive events in different orders than the remote user, leading to divergent states.\n\n### 3.3 Required Plugin API Changes\n\nTo safely support collaboration, the following changes would be necessary:\n\n#### A. Versioned State Access\n\n```typescript\n// New: IPluginService.ts addition\ninterface CollaborativeContext<VM = any> extends CanvasNodeContext<VM> {\n  /** Current logical clock/version for conflict detection */\n  readonly stateVersion: VectorClock | number;\n\n  /** Request a consistent snapshot that won't change during operation */\n  acquireSnapshot(): Promise<ImmutableNodeSnapshot>;\n\n  /** Submit changes via operational transform */\n  submitOperation(op: Operation): Promise<OperationResult>;\n}\n```\n\n#### B. Optimistic Update Pattern\n\n```typescript\n// New hook addition for plugins\ninterface NodeLifecycleHooks {\n  // Existing\n  onCreate(ctx: CanvasNodeContext): void;\n\n  // New: Called when remote operation arrives\n  onRemoteOperation?(ctx: CanvasNodeContext, op: RemoteOperation): void;\n\n  // New: Called when local operation conflicts with remote\n  onConflict?(ctx: CanvasNodeContext, conflict: ConflictInfo): Resolution;\n}\n```\n\n#### C. Presence Awareness\n\n```typescript\n// New API surface in @paletteflow/sdk\ninterface CollaborationAPI {\n  /** Other users currently viewing/editing this node */\n  getPresence(nodeId: string): UserPresence[];\n\n  /** Subscribe to presence changes */\n  onPresenceChange(callback: (presence: UserPresence[]) => void): Unsubscribe;\n\n  /** Show cursor/selection of remote users */\n  showRemoteCursor(userId: string, position: Vector2D): void;\n}\n```\n\n#### D. Operation Batching\n\n```typescript\n// Modification to IPluginService.ts\ninterface IPluginService {\n  // New: Batch multiple operations into atomic unit\n  beginOperationBatch(nodeId: string): OperationBatch;\n\n  // Existing hook runner, now collaboration-aware\n  runHook<TName extends PluginHookName>(\n    hook: TName,\n    args: PluginHookArguments<TName>,\n    options?: { collaborative?: boolean }\n  ): Promise<PluginHookResult<TName>[]>;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Resolution Strategy\n\n### 4.1 Current State of Domain Entities\n\nExamining the core domain entities for conflict-resolution properties:\n\n#### Workspace (`src/core/domain/entities/Workspace.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 182-189\nprivate _id: WorkspaceId;\nprivate _name: string;\nprivate _createdAt: Date;\nprivate _updatedAt: Date;      // Simple timestamp\nprivate _state: WorkspaceState;\nprivate _metadata: Record<string, unknown>;\nprivate _canvases: Map<CanvasId, Canvas>;\nprivate _version: number;       // Simple integer version\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Has a `_version: number` field (line 189, 244-246) that is incremented in `touch()` (line 400-403)\n- Uses simple timestamps (`createdAt`, `updatedAt`) - **no vector clocks**\n- No user/session tracking for concurrent modification detection\n\n#### Node (`src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 82-87\nexport interface NodeMetadata {\n  readonly label: string;\n  readonly createdAt: Date;\n  readonly updatedAt: Date;    // Simple timestamp\n  readonly tags: ReadonlyArray<string>;\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only has `updatedAt` timestamp - **no version number**\n- No `lastModifiedBy` or session identifier\n- No operation history or tombstone markers\n\n#### Canvas (`src/core/domain/entities/Canvas.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 53-60\ninterface CanvasProps {\n  title: string;\n  themeId?: UniqueEntityID;\n  nodes?: Map<string, Node>;\n  links?: Map<string, Link>;\n  createdAt?: Date;\n  updatedAt?: Date;            // Simple timestamp only\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only simple timestamps\n- No version or clock properties\n\n#### Link (`src/core/domain/entities/Link.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 34-43\nexport interface LinkProps {\n  sourceNodeId: UniqueEntityID;\n  targetNodeId: UniqueEntityID;\n  type: LinkType;\n  label?: string;\n  directed?: boolean;\n  metadata?: Record<string, unknown>;\n  createdAt?: Date;\n  updatedAt?: Date;            // Simple timestamp only\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only simple timestamps - **no version tracking**\n\n### 4.2 Summary: Conflict Resolution Support\n\n| Entity | Version Number | Vector Clock | Last-Modified-By | Operation Log |\n|--------|---------------|--------------|------------------|---------------|\n| Workspace | `_version: number` | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Node | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Canvas | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Link | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n\n**Critical Finding:** The entities lack the fundamental metadata required for distributed conflict resolution:\n- No **vector clocks** or **Lamport timestamps** for causal ordering\n- No **operation identifiers** for OT (Operational Transform)\n- No **actor/replica IDs** for CRDT implementations\n- The Workspace's simple integer `version` only supports optimistic locking, not merge resolution\n\n### 4.3 Recommended Location for Conflict Resolution Logic\n\nBased on the Clean Architecture principles used in PaletteFlow Studio, **conflict resolution logic should be implemented in the `core/application/use-cases` layer**.\n\n#### Justification:\n\n1. **Domain Layer Purity**: The `core/domain/entities` layer should remain focused on business invariants, not synchronization concerns. Adding CRDT or OT logic here would violate the principle that \"domain entities know nothing about persistence, rendering or UI frameworks\" (`Canvas.ts:8`).\n\n2. **Use Case Orchestration**: The use-case layer already handles:\n   - Transaction management (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:156`)\n   - Plugin hook coordination (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:142-152`)\n   - Event publishing (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:162-168`)\n\n   Conflict resolution is similarly a cross-cutting orchestration concern.\n\n3. **Repository Interface Flexibility**: The `IWorkspaceRepository` already supports different storage backends. A collaboration-enabled repository could implement `observeById()` (line 169) to provide real-time updates from a server.\n\n4. **Adapter Independence**: Implementing conflict resolution as a use-case service allows different sync backends (WebSocket, WebRTC, P2P) to be swapped via the adapter layer without changing business logic.\n\n#### Recommended Architecture:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502                      Presentation Layer                      \u2502\n\u2502  (Renderer: React + Redux, NodeComponent, CanvasView)       \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502                      Application Layer                       \u2502\n\u2502  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  NEW: CollaborationService                          \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  - CRDT/OT engine                                   \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  - Operation queue                                  \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  - Conflict resolution                              \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518    \u2502\n\u2502  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510    \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502                       Domain Layer                           \u2502\n\u2502  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  Entities: Workspace, Canvas, Node, Link            \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  NEW: Add version vectors, operation IDs            \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  FileSystemWorkspaceRepository (local fallback)     \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502 Recommended CRDT Approach for Canvas Data:\n\nGiven the nature of canvas operations (positions, content, links), a hybrid approach would work best:\n\n1. **Positional data (Node.position)**: Use a Last-Writer-Wins Register (LWW-Register) with Lamport timestamps. Position conflicts are resolved by most recent write.\n\n2. **Text content (Node.content for markdown/code)**: Use Yjs or Automerge CRDT for character-level merging of text content.\n\n3. **Structural data (Canvas.nodes, Canvas.links)**: Use Observed-Remove Set (OR-Set) CRDT to handle concurrent add/remove operations.\n\n4. **Metadata (labels, tags)**: LWW-Register for simple values, OR-Set for collections.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Summary of Key Findings\n\n### Architecture Strengths for Collaboration Transition:\n\n1. **Clean Architecture** enables swapping the persistence layer without affecting domain/use-case logic\n2. **Event-driven design** with domain events provides a foundation for operation broadcasting\n3. **Repository interface** (`IWorkspaceRepository`) is already designed for multiple backend implementations\n4. **Observable support** (`observeById()` returning RxJS Observable) anticipates real-time updates\n\n### Critical Gaps Requiring Address:\n\n1. **Source of Truth Migration**: Must move from local file system to server-based or P2P shared state\n2. **Entity Version Metadata**: Add vector clocks or logical timestamps to all domain entities\n3. **Operation-Based Mutations**: Refactor from state-based persistence to operation-based sync\n4. **Plugin API Evolution**: Add collaborative-aware hooks and snapshot isolation\n5. **IPC Architecture**: Add server push capability alongside request-response pattern\n\n### Estimated Effort (Relative):\n\n| Component | Effort | Risk |\n|-----------|--------|------|\n| Domain entity versioning | Medium | Low |\n| Collaboration service (CRDT) | High | Medium |\n| Server/sync infrastructure | High | High |\n| Plugin API changes | Medium | High (ecosystem impact) |\n| UI presence indicators | Low | Low |\n| Testing/migration | High | Medium |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Files Referenced\n\n| Purpose | File Path |\n|---------|-----------|\n| Architecture overview | `docs/architecture.md` |\n| Workspace repository interface | `src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| File system repository | `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Workspace entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Workspace.ts` |\n| Node entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts` |\n| Canvas entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Canvas.ts` |\n| Link entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Link.ts` |\n| IPC channels | `src/main/ipc/channels.ts` |\n| Workspace IPC handlers | `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts` |\n| Renderer IPC bridge | `src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts` |\n| Redux store | `src/renderer/state/store.ts` |\n| ViewModel hook | `src/renderer/hooks/useViewModel.ts` |\n| Node UI component | `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx` |\n| UpdateNodePosition use case | `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts` |\n| Plugin service interface | `src/core/application/services/IPluginService.ts` |\n| Event bus interface | `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts` |\n| Node API documentation | `docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md` |\n| Main process entry | `src/main/index.ts` |\n",

  "content": "# Architectural Analysis Report: Real-Time Collaboration for PaletteFlow Studio\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nPaletteFlow Studio is a single-user desktop application built on Electron with a Clean Architecture design. This analysis evaluates the feasibility of adding real-time multi-user collaboration and outlines the necessary architectural changes. The current architecture, while well-designed for single-user scenarios, presents significant challenges for collaboration due to its file-system-centric persistence, synchronous plugin APIs, and absence of conflict resolution mechanisms in domain entities.\n\n---\n\n## 1. State Management & Source of Truth\n\n### 1.1 Current Source of Truth\n\n**The primary source of truth for workspace data is the local file system.**\n\nThe persistence layer is implemented in `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`:\n\n```typescript\n// src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:35-36\nconst WORKSPACE_FILE_NAME = 'workspace.pfws';  // gzipped JSON\nconst MANIFEST_FILE_NAME = 'manifest.json';    // plain JSON\n```\n\nEach workspace is stored as a gzipped JSON file (`workspace.pfws`) in a directory under the user's configured root. The repository provides:\n- **Atomic writes** via write-to-temp-then-rename pattern (lines 147-153)\n- **File watching** for external changes (lines 244-255)\n- **Event emission** for workspace lifecycle events (lines 276-293)\n\nThe `IWorkspaceRepository` interface (`src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts:131-194`) defines the port contract that allows this implementation to be swapped, though currently only the file-system adapter exists.\n\n### 1.2 State Management Strategy\n\n**Main Process:**\n- The main process acts as the **orchestration layer** and doesn't maintain significant application state\n- Use cases are instantiated per-request in IPC handlers (`src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts:85-86`)\n- State flows through the repository layer to the file system\n- Domain events are published via `DomainEventBus` for cross-cutting concerns\n\n**Renderer Process:**\n- Uses **Redux Toolkit** with the store defined in `src/renderer/state/store.ts`\n- The store holds UI-centric slices: `workspace`, `ui`, and `pluginHub` (lines 71-75)\n- State synchronization happens via:\n  1. **Cross-window middleware** (`crossWindowSyncMiddleware`, lines 154-173) that broadcasts Redux actions via IPC\n  2. **IPC listener** for `main:action-broadcast` that re-dispatches actions from other windows (lines 243-250)\n  3. **State replacement** mechanism via `main:state-replace` for loading workspace files (lines 257-263)\n\n**Synchronization Mechanism:**\nThe current sync is **event-driven but eventually consistent**:\n```typescript\n// src/renderer/state/store.ts:243-250\nipcRenderer.on(\n  'main:action-broadcast',\n  (_: IpcRendererEvent, { originId, action }) => {\n    if (originId !== window.__WINDOW_ID__) {\n      store.dispatch(action as AnyAction);\n    }\n  }\n);\n```\n\n### 1.3 Suitability for Multi-User Real-Time Environment\n\n**This model is NOT suitable for real-time collaboration for several reasons:**\n\n1. **Single-Point File Lock**: The file system cannot serve as a shared source of truth for multiple simultaneous users. File-level locking (mentioned at line 77: \"Basic optimistic locking to avoid clobbering concurrent saves\") only works within a single machine.\n\n2. **No Server-Side Authority**: There is no central server to act as the authoritative state holder. Each user's local file system is their truth, creating inevitable divergence.\n\n3. **Stale Read Problem**: When User A modifies a node, User B's renderer process has no mechanism to receive that update - the file system watcher only monitors local changes.\n\n4. **No Ordering Guarantees**: The Redux action broadcasting assumes all participants receive actions in the same order, which cannot be guaranteed across network boundaries.\n\n5. **Optimistic Updates Without Rollback**: The current optimistic concurrency control (`WorkspaceConflictError` in `IWorkspaceRepository.ts:100-104`) is designed for local multi-window scenarios, not distributed conflict detection.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Data Flow for Mutations\n\n### 2.1 Tracing a Node Move Operation\n\nLet's trace the complete data flow when a user drags a node on the canvas:\n\n#### Step 1: UI Event Capture (Renderer - React Component)\n\n**File:** `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx:120-126`\n\n```typescript\nconst handlePointerMove = useCallback<React.PointerEventHandler<HTMLDivElement>>(\n  (e) => {\n    if (!isDragging) return;\n    nodeVM.setPosition(e.clientX - dragOrigin.current.x, e.clientY - dragOrigin.current.y);\n  },\n  [isDragging, nodeVM],\n);\n```\n\nThe `NodeComponent` captures pointer events and calls `nodeVM.setPosition()` on the ViewModel.\n\n#### Step 2: ViewModel Update (Renderer - MobX Observable)\n\n**File:** Referenced as `NodeViewModel` from `src/renderer/viewModels/NodeViewModel`\n\nThe ViewModel (likely MobX-based given the `observer` wrapper at line 243) updates its internal observable state and triggers a re-render.\n\n#### Step 3: IPC Bridge Call (Renderer to Main)\n\nThe ViewModel calls through the IPC bridge. Based on the bridge structure (`src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts`), a node position update would invoke something like:\n\n```typescript\n// src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts - Pattern for canvas operations\nipcRenderer.invoke(channel, payload)\n```\n\n#### Step 4: IPC Handler Reception (Main Process)\n\n**File:** `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts`\n\nThe handler receives the request and instantiates the appropriate use case.\n\n#### Step 5: Use Case Execution (Core Application Layer)\n\n**File:** `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts:108-183`\n\n```typescript\nasync execute(dto: UpdateNodePositionDTO): Promise<Result<UpdateNodePositionError, void>> {\n    // Validation\n    if (!this.isFiniteCoordinate(dto.x, dto.y)) { ... }\n\n    // Fetch entities\n    const canvas = await this.canvasRepo.findById(dto.canvasId);\n    const node = await this.nodeRepo.findById(dto.nodeId);\n\n    // Plugin hook for veto/transformation\n    const pluginDisposition = await this.pluginHost.hooks.beforeNodeMove.reduce(...);\n\n    // Execute in transaction\n    await this.tx.runInTransaction(async () => {\n        node.moveTo(pluginDisposition.x, pluginDisposition.y);\n        await this.nodeRepo.save(node);\n\n        // Publish domain event\n        await this.eventBus.publish(new NodePositionUpdated({...}));\n    });\n\n    // Post-move plugin hooks\n    await this.pluginHost.hooks.afterNodeMove.forEach(...);\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Domain Entity Mutation\n\n**File:** `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts:223-230`\n\n```typescript\npublic moveTo(position: Vector2D): this {\n    if (Number.isNaN(position.x) || Number.isNaN(position.y)) {\n        throw new Error('Position must contain valid numbers.');\n    }\n    this._position = { x: position.x, y: position.y };\n    this._touch();  // Updates metadata.updatedAt\n    return this._registerEvent('NodeMoved', { position: this._position });\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Repository Persistence\n\n**File:** `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:132-174`\n\nThe `save()` method:\n1. Creates workspace directory if needed\n2. Serializes workspace to JSON\n3. Compresses with gzip\n4. Writes atomically via temp file + rename\n\n#### Step 8: Domain Event Propagation\n\n**File:** `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts:102-105`\n\n```typescript\npublish<E extends DomainEvent>(\n  event: E,\n  options?: PublishOptions,\n): Promise<void>;\n```\n\nThe `NodePositionUpdated` event is broadcast to subscribers (analytics, plugin SDK, UI observers).\n\n### 2.2 Key Components Summary\n\n| Layer | Component | File Path |\n|-------|-----------|-----------|\n| UI | NodeComponent | `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx` |\n| ViewModel | NodeViewModel | `src/renderer/viewModels/NodeViewModel` |\n| IPC Bridge | IPCBridge | `src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts` |\n| IPC Handler | workspaceHandlers | `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts` |\n| Use Case | UpdateNodePosition | `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts` |\n| Domain Entity | Node | `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts` |\n| Repository Port | IWorkspaceRepository | `src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Repository Impl | FileSystemWorkspaceRepository | `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Event Bus | IEventBus | `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts` |\n\n### 2.3 Limitations for Concurrent Users\n\n1. **Request-Response IPC Model**: The current `ipcMain.handle()` / `ipcRenderer.invoke()` pattern (`src/main/ipc/channels.ts:176`) is designed for single-client request-response. There's no built-in mechanism for the main process to push updates to renderers that didn't initiate the request.\n\n2. **Sequential Save Queue**: The `saveQueue` in `workspaceHandlers.ts:50-51` serializes saves per workspace, but only within a single main process. Multiple users would bypass this queue.\n\n3. **No Delta Transmission**: The entire workspace is serialized and persisted on each save. For collaboration, we'd need operation-level (delta) transmission.\n\n4. **Blocking Transactions**: The `TransactionManager` used in `UpdateNodePosition.ts:156-169` provides local atomicity but cannot coordinate distributed transactions.\n\n5. **Plugin Veto Race Conditions**: The `beforeNodeMove` hook (line 142-152) runs sequentially through plugins. In a multi-user scenario, Plugin A might veto User A's move while simultaneously allowing User B's conflicting move.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Impact on the Plugin System\n\n### 3.1 Current Plugin API Architecture\n\nThe plugin system is defined through:\n- **Service Interface:** `src/core/application/services/IPluginService.ts`\n- **SDK Documentation:** `docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md`\n\nKey characteristics:\n\n1. **Synchronous-Style Data Access**: The Node API (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:336-344`) provides direct access to ViewModel state:\n   ```typescript\n   interface CanvasNodeContext<VM = any> {\n     readonly id: string;\n     readonly vm: VM;  // Direct ViewModel access\n     emit<E extends NodeEvent>(event: E): void;\n     on<E extends NodeEvent>(type: E['type'], cb: (event: E) => void): Unsubscribe;\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Hook-Based Extension**: Plugins implement lifecycle hooks (`onCreate`, `onMount`, `onUpdate`, `onDestroy`) that receive a \"hot-scoped\" context (line 333-344).\n\n3. **State Machine Pattern**: Node logic is encapsulated in XState-inspired machines (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:178-206`) with mutable context.\n\n4. **Sandboxed Execution**: Plugins run in `vm2` sandboxes per the architecture doc (line 232).\n\n### 3.2 Collaboration Impact on Plugin Stability\n\n**The introduction of real-time collaboration would significantly destabilize the plugin ecosystem:**\n\n1. **Stale Context Problem**: The `CanvasNodeContext.vm` reference assumes stable, locally-controlled state. With collaboration:\n   ```typescript\n   // Plugin code\n   const oldPosition = ctx.vm.position;  // {x: 100, y: 100}\n   // ... another user moves the node remotely ...\n   ctx.vm.updateContent(...);  // Operates on stale position assumption\n   ```\n\n2. **Hook Ordering Non-Determinism**: The `beforeNodeMove` reducer pattern (from `UpdateNodePosition.ts:142-144`) assumes sequential plugin execution. With concurrent users, two hooks might run on different initial states:\n   ```typescript\n   // Current single-user flow\n   pluginHost.hooks.beforeNodeMove.reduce(\n     async (incomingPosition, hook) => hook(node, await incomingPosition),\n     Promise.resolve({ x: dto.x, y: dto.y })\n   );\n   ```\n\n3. **Event Race Conditions**: The event bus (`docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md:356-366`) uses namespaced events for inter-node communication. Concurrent modifications could trigger event storms or out-of-order delivery.\n\n4. **State Machine Divergence**: The `NodeStateMachine` pattern expects deterministic state transitions. Remote operations could cause local machines to receive events in different orders than the remote user, leading to divergent states.\n\n### 3.3 Required Plugin API Changes\n\nTo safely support collaboration, the following changes would be necessary:\n\n#### A. Versioned State Access\n\n```typescript\n// New: IPluginService.ts addition\ninterface CollaborativeContext<VM = any> extends CanvasNodeContext<VM> {\n  /** Current logical clock/version for conflict detection */\n  readonly stateVersion: VectorClock | number;\n\n  /** Request a consistent snapshot that won't change during operation */\n  acquireSnapshot(): Promise<ImmutableNodeSnapshot>;\n\n  /** Submit changes via operational transform */\n  submitOperation(op: Operation): Promise<OperationResult>;\n}\n```\n\n#### B. Optimistic Update Pattern\n\n```typescript\n// New hook addition for plugins\ninterface NodeLifecycleHooks {\n  // Existing\n  onCreate(ctx: CanvasNodeContext): void;\n\n  // New: Called when remote operation arrives\n  onRemoteOperation?(ctx: CanvasNodeContext, op: RemoteOperation): void;\n\n  // New: Called when local operation conflicts with remote\n  onConflict?(ctx: CanvasNodeContext, conflict: ConflictInfo): Resolution;\n}\n```\n\n#### C. Presence Awareness\n\n```typescript\n// New API surface in @paletteflow/sdk\ninterface CollaborationAPI {\n  /** Other users currently viewing/editing this node */\n  getPresence(nodeId: string): UserPresence[];\n\n  /** Subscribe to presence changes */\n  onPresenceChange(callback: (presence: UserPresence[]) => void): Unsubscribe;\n\n  /** Show cursor/selection of remote users */\n  showRemoteCursor(userId: string, position: Vector2D): void;\n}\n```\n\n#### D. Operation Batching\n\n```typescript\n// Modification to IPluginService.ts\ninterface IPluginService {\n  // New: Batch multiple operations into atomic unit\n  beginOperationBatch(nodeId: string): OperationBatch;\n\n  // Existing hook runner, now collaboration-aware\n  runHook<TName extends PluginHookName>(\n    hook: TName,\n    args: PluginHookArguments<TName>,\n    options?: { collaborative?: boolean }\n  ): Promise<PluginHookResult<TName>[]>;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Resolution Strategy\n\n### 4.1 Current State of Domain Entities\n\nExamining the core domain entities for conflict-resolution properties:\n\n#### Workspace (`src/core/domain/entities/Workspace.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 182-189\nprivate _id: WorkspaceId;\nprivate _name: string;\nprivate _createdAt: Date;\nprivate _updatedAt: Date;      // Simple timestamp\nprivate _state: WorkspaceState;\nprivate _metadata: Record<string, unknown>;\nprivate _canvases: Map<CanvasId, Canvas>;\nprivate _version: number;       // Simple integer version\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Has a `_version: number` field (line 189, 244-246) that is incremented in `touch()` (line 400-403)\n- Uses simple timestamps (`createdAt`, `updatedAt`) - **no vector clocks**\n- No user/session tracking for concurrent modification detection\n\n#### Node (`src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 82-87\nexport interface NodeMetadata {\n  readonly label: string;\n  readonly createdAt: Date;\n  readonly updatedAt: Date;    // Simple timestamp\n  readonly tags: ReadonlyArray<string>;\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only has `updatedAt` timestamp - **no version number**\n- No `lastModifiedBy` or session identifier\n- No operation history or tombstone markers\n\n#### Canvas (`src/core/domain/entities/Canvas.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 53-60\ninterface CanvasProps {\n  title: string;\n  themeId?: UniqueEntityID;\n  nodes?: Map<string, Node>;\n  links?: Map<string, Link>;\n  createdAt?: Date;\n  updatedAt?: Date;            // Simple timestamp only\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only simple timestamps\n- No version or clock properties\n\n#### Link (`src/core/domain/entities/Link.ts`)\n\n```typescript\n// Lines 34-43\nexport interface LinkProps {\n  sourceNodeId: UniqueEntityID;\n  targetNodeId: UniqueEntityID;\n  type: LinkType;\n  label?: string;\n  directed?: boolean;\n  metadata?: Record<string, unknown>;\n  createdAt?: Date;\n  updatedAt?: Date;            // Simple timestamp only\n}\n```\n\n**Findings:**\n- Only simple timestamps - **no version tracking**\n\n### 4.2 Summary: Conflict Resolution Support\n\n| Entity | Version Number | Vector Clock | Last-Modified-By | Operation Log |\n|--------|---------------|--------------|------------------|---------------|\n| Workspace | `_version: number` | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Node | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Canvas | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n| Link | No | No | No | Domain events only |\n\n**Critical Finding:** The entities lack the fundamental metadata required for distributed conflict resolution:\n- No **vector clocks** or **Lamport timestamps** for causal ordering\n- No **operation identifiers** for OT (Operational Transform)\n- No **actor/replica IDs** for CRDT implementations\n- The Workspace's simple integer `version` only supports optimistic locking, not merge resolution\n\n### 4.3 Recommended Location for Conflict Resolution Logic\n\nBased on the Clean Architecture principles used in PaletteFlow Studio, **conflict resolution logic should be implemented in the `core/application/use-cases` layer**.\n\n#### Justification:\n\n1. **Domain Layer Purity**: The `core/domain/entities` layer should remain focused on business invariants, not synchronization concerns. Adding CRDT or OT logic here would violate the principle that \"domain entities know nothing about persistence, rendering or UI frameworks\" (`Canvas.ts:8`).\n\n2. **Use Case Orchestration**: The use-case layer already handles:\n   - Transaction management (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:156`)\n   - Plugin hook coordination (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:142-152`)\n   - Event publishing (`UpdateNodePosition.ts:162-168`)\n\n   Conflict resolution is similarly a cross-cutting orchestration concern.\n\n3. **Repository Interface Flexibility**: The `IWorkspaceRepository` already supports different storage backends. A collaboration-enabled repository could implement `observeById()` (line 169) to provide real-time updates from a server.\n\n4. **Adapter Independence**: Implementing conflict resolution as a use-case service allows different sync backends (WebSocket, WebRTC, P2P) to be swapped via the adapter layer without changing business logic.\n\n#### Recommended Architecture:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502                      Presentation Layer                      \u2502\n\u2502  (Renderer: React + Redux, NodeComponent, CanvasView)       \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Recommended CRDT Approach for Canvas Data:\n\nGiven the nature of canvas operations (positions, content, links), a hybrid approach would work best:\n\n1. **Positional data (Node.position)**: Use a Last-Writer-Wins Register (LWW-Register) with Lamport timestamps. Position conflicts are resolved by most recent write.\n\n2. **Text content (Node.content for markdown/code)**: Use Yjs or Automerge CRDT for character-level merging of text content.\n\n3. **Structural data (Canvas.nodes, Canvas.links)**: Use Observed-Remove Set (OR-Set) CRDT to handle concurrent add/remove operations.\n\n4. **Metadata (labels, tags)**: LWW-Register for simple values, OR-Set for collections.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Summary of Key Findings\n\n### Architecture Strengths for Collaboration Transition:\n\n1. **Clean Architecture** enables swapping the persistence layer without affecting domain/use-case logic\n2. **Event-driven design** with domain events provides a foundation for operation broadcasting\n3. **Repository interface** (`IWorkspaceRepository`) is already designed for multiple backend implementations\n4. **Observable support** (`observeById()` returning RxJS Observable) anticipates real-time updates\n\n### Critical Gaps Requiring Address:\n\n1. **Source of Truth Migration**: Must move from local file system to server-based or P2P shared state\n2. **Entity Version Metadata**: Add vector clocks or logical timestamps to all domain entities\n3. **Operation-Based Mutations**: Refactor from state-based persistence to operation-based sync\n4. **Plugin API Evolution**: Add collaborative-aware hooks and snapshot isolation\n5. **IPC Architecture**: Add server push capability alongside request-response pattern\n\n### Estimated Effort (Relative):\n\n| Component | Effort | Risk |\n|-----------|--------|------|\n| Domain entity versioning | Medium | Low |\n| Collaboration service (CRDT) | High | Medium |\n| Server/sync infrastructure | High | High |\n| Plugin API changes | Medium | High (ecosystem impact) |\n| UI presence indicators | Low | Low |\n| Testing/migration | High | Medium |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Files Referenced\n\n| Purpose | File Path |\n|---------|-----------|\n| Architecture overview | `docs/architecture.md` |\n| Workspace repository interface | `src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| File system repository | `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts` |\n| Workspace entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Workspace.ts` |\n| Node entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Node.ts` |\n| Canvas entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Canvas.ts` |\n| Link entity | `src/core/domain/entities/Link.ts` |\n| IPC channels | `src/main/ipc/channels.ts` |\n| Workspace IPC handlers | `src/main/ipc/handlers/workspaceHandlers.ts` |\n| Renderer IPC bridge | `src/renderer/ipc/bridge.ts` |\n| Redux store | `src/renderer/state/store.ts` |\n| ViewModel hook | `src/renderer/hooks/useViewModel.ts` |\n| Node UI component | `src/renderer/components/canvas/NodeComponent.tsx` |\n| UpdateNodePosition use case | `src/core/application/use-cases/node/UpdateNodePosition.ts` |\n| Plugin service interface | `src/core/application/services/IPluginService.ts` |\n| Event bus interface | `src/core/application/services/IEventBus.ts` |\n| Node API documentation | `docs/plugin-api/reference/node-api.md` |\n| Main process entry | `src/main/index.ts` |\n",

This analysis evaluates the feasibility of adding real-time multi-user collaboration and outlines the necessary architectural changes. # Architectural Analysis Report: Real-Time Collaboration for PaletteFlow Studio

## Executive Summary

PaletteFlow Studio is a single-user desktop application built on Electron with a Clean Architecture design. This analysis evaluates the feasibility of adding real-time multi-user collaboration and outlines the necessary architectural changes. The current architecture, while well-designed for single-user scenarios, presents significant challenges for collaboration due to its file-system-centric persistence, synchronous plugin APIs, and absence of conflict resolution mechanisms in domain entities.

---

## 1. State Management & Source of Truth

### 1.1 Current Source of Truth

**The primary source of truth for workspace data is the local file system.**

The persistence layer is implemented in `src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts`:

```typescript
// src/adapters/repositories/FileSystemWorkspaceRepository.ts:35-36
const WORKSPACE_FILE_NAME = 'workspace.pfws';  // gzipped JSON
const MANIFEST_FILE_NAME = 'manifest.json';    // plain JSON
```

Each workspace is stored as a gzipped JSON file (`workspace.pfws`) in a directory under the user's configured root. The repository provides:
- **Atomic writes** via write-to-temp-then-rename pattern (lines 147-153)
- **File watching** for external changes (lines 244-255)
- **Event emission** for workspace lifecycle events (lines 276-293)

The `IWorkspaceRepository` interface (`src/core/application/repositories/IWorkspaceRepository.ts:131-194`) defines the port contract that allows this implementation to be swapped, though currently only the file-system adapter exists.

### 1.2 State Management Strategy

**Main Process:**
- The main process acts as the **orchestration layer** and doesn't maintain significant applic
